The Obligation of 'Ushr on Honey and the Dispute on Nisab
Ruling on 'ushr for honey with proofs and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'ushr for honey, identify the proofs (hadith and qiyas), and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's position (no nisab) and the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the nisab.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: honey's 'ushr is due on any amount; Sahibayn require a minimum threshold.

This lesson examines the obligation of 'ushr (tithe) on honey. The Hanafi school is unanimous that 'ushr is wajib on honey, but there is a notable intra-school dispute regarding whether a minimum quantity (nisab) is required for the obligation. The text from Al-Hidayah presents the proofs and the differing views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the common ground
Identify that all Hanafi imams agree 'ushr is wajib on honey.
The disagreement is only on nisab.
2
Review the proof texts
Examine the hadith of Abu Hurairah and the qiyas on fruits.
Note the hadith is ahad, so the ruling is wajib not fard.
3
Find the point of ikhtilaf
Pinpoint that Abu Hanifa holds no nisab, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad each propose different minimum thresholds.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
List each imam's position
State Abu Hanifa: no nisab; Abu Yusuf: three narrations (value of 5 wasqs, 10 mashkizahs, 5 manns); Muhammad: 5 farqs.
Also note the similar dispute on sugarcane.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text indicates that the position of Abu Hanifa (no nisab) is the relied-upon view in Al-Hidayah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text

علیہ وسلم کو دیا کرتے تھے اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم ان کی وادی کی ان کے لئے حفاظت کرتے تھے پس جب حضرت امیر المومنین عمر بن الخطاب کا عہد خلافت آیا اور آپ نے سفیان بن عبد اللہ ثقفی کو عامل مقرر تم کو عشر دیں جو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو دیا کرتے تھے تو تم ان کی وادی کی حفاظت کرو۔ ورنہ ان مکھیوں اور لوگوں کے درمیان تخلیہ کر دو۔ اس جواب کے بعد ان لوگوں نے عشر دینا شروع کر دیا حضرت عمر کے جواب کا حاصل یہ تھا کہ اگر یہ لوگ عشر دیں تو ان کی وادیوں کی ان کے واسطے حفاظت کرو۔ ورنہ جو چاہے شہد نکال لیجائے۔ بہر حال اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بنو شبابہ کے لوگ دس مشکیزوں میں سے ایک مشکیزہ عشر دیا کرتے تھے ایک مشکیزہ پچاس رطل کا ہوتا ہے۔ تیسری روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر شہد پانچ من ہو تو اس میں عشر واجب ہو جائے گا امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ پانچ فرق نصاب ہے یعنی پانچ فرق شہد میں عشر واجب ہوتا ہے اور ایک فرق چھتیں رطل کا ہوتا ہے کیونکہ جن پیمانوں سے شہد کا اندازہ کیا جاتا ہے ان میں سب سے اعلیٰ پیالہ فرق ہی ہے اور گنے میں بھی امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان یہی اختلاف ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک گنے کی قیمت اگر پانچ وسق کو پہنچ جائے تو عشر واجب ہو جائے گا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اگر پانچ من گنا ہو تو اس میں عشر واجب ہوگا۔ اور پہاڑوں میں جو پھل اور شہد پلایا جائے اس میں بھی عشر واجب ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اس میں عشر واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ وجوب عشر کا سبب نہیں پایا گیا اور وہ زمین کا نامی ہونا ہے۔ زیادہ بہتر تھا کہ یہ کہا جاتا کہ وجوب عشر کا سبب مملوکہ زمین ہے اور ظاہر الروایۃ یعنی عشر واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو مقصود ہے وہ حاصل ہے یعنی پیداوار حاصل ہے پس جب پیدا اور موجود ہے تو اس میں عشر بھی واجب ہوگا۔
Our proof is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'From Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, wrote to the people of Yemen: Indeed, on honey is the 'ushr (tithe).' That is, the Prophet, peace be upon him, wrote to the people of Yemen that 'ushr is obligatory on honey. The second proof is that bees eat flowers and fruits, as Allah Almighty says: 'Then eat of all the fruits.' And on flowers and fruits, 'ushr is obligatory, so what is produced from them, i.e., honey, will also have 'ushr obligatory, unlike the silkworm which eats mulberry leaves, and on leaves 'ushr is not obligatory, so what is produced from it, i.e., silk, will also not have 'ushr obligatory. The author of Al-Hidayah said that 'ushr is obligatory on honey, whether the honey is little or much, because Imam Abu Hanifa does not consider a nisab for the obligation of 'ushr. There are three narrations from Imam Abu Yusuf about this: One is that if honey is equivalent in value to five wasqs, then 'ushr is obligatory; this is the original view of Imam Abu Yusuf. Second, that if the quantity of honey is equal to ten mashkizahs, then 'ushr is obligatory; the proof is the hadith of Bani Shababah. In Al-Inayah, this hadith is that a tribe of Bani Jurhum called Bani Shiba had beehives. They used to give one mashkizah out of every ten to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, protected their valley for them. When the caliphate of Umar ibn al-Khattab came, he appointed Sufyan ibn Abdullah al-Thaqafi as governor. Those people refused to pay 'ushr. Sufyan ibn Abdullah wrote to Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, and Umar replied: 'Bees are rain-bees; Allah takes them wherever He wishes. If they give you the 'ushr that they used to give to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, then protect their valley. Otherwise, create a void between these bees and the people.' After this reply, they began to pay 'ushr. The summary of Umar's reply was: if they give 'ushr, protect their valleys for them; otherwise, let anyone take the honey. In any case, it is learned from this hadith that the people of Bani Shababah used to give one mashkizah out of ten as 'ushr. One mashkizah is fifty ratls. The third narration is that if honey is five manns, then 'ushr is obligatory. It is narrated from Imam Muhammad that the nisab is five farqs: that is, 'ushr is obligatory on five farqs of honey, and one farq is sixty ratls, because among the measurements used to estimate honey, the highest measure is the farq. And in sugarcane as well, there is the same difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad: according to Imam Abu Yusuf, if the price of sugarcane reaches five wasqs, then 'ushr is obligatory; and according to Imam Muhammad, if there are five manns of sugarcane, then 'ushr is obligatory. And on mountain fruits and honey that is watered, 'ushr is also obligatory. And from Abu Yusuf there is a narration that 'ushr is not obligatory on it, because the cause of the obligation of 'ushr is not found, and that is the land being fertile. It would have been better to say that the cause of the obligation of 'ushr is owned land. And Zahir al-Riwayah: the proof of the obligation of 'ushr is that what is intended is attained, i.e., produce is present; so when it is produced and present, then 'ushr is obligatory on it.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage combines a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by establishing the obligation of 'ushr on honey through two proofs: first, a hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet wrote to the people of Yemen commanding 'ushr on honey; second, a qiyas argument that bees feed on fruits and flowers, which themselves are subject to 'ushr, so honey should also be subject to 'ushr, analogously to fruit but unlike silk which comes from leaves not subject to 'ushr. The author then states Abu Hanifa's position that 'ushr on honey is obligatory regardless of quantity—no nisab is required. This is followed by the three narrations from Abu Yusuf: (1) nisab of value equivalent to five wasqs; (2) nisab of ten mashkizahs (based on the practice of Bani Shababah, with each mashkizah being 50 ratls); (3) nisab of five manns (from another narration). Imam Muhammad holds that nisab is five farqs (each farq being 60 ratls). The passage then notes that similar ikhtilaf exists for sugarcane. Finally, a minority narration from Abu Yusuf denies 'ushr on mountain produce, but the author clarifies that Zahir al-Riwayah affirms it.

Key Terms
العشر (al-‘ushr): The tenth part of produce or honey that is due as zakat/charity.
نصاب (nisāb): The minimum threshold of wealth or produce that must be reached for obligation of zakat or 'ushr.
وسق (wasq): A measure of volume, approximately 60 sa' or 130-160 kg.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the proof cited by the author for the obligation of 'ushr on honey?
A) Quranic verse on fruits.
B) Hadith of Abu Hurairah.
C) Practice of Umar.
D) Consensus of the Sahaba.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa holds that 'ushr on honey is wajib without a nisab, while the Sahibayn require a minimum threshold.

No Deduction of Labor and Animal Expenses from 'Ushr
Ruling that expenses are not deductible from 'ushr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that labor and animal expenses are not deductible from 'ushr and apply it to a sample calculation.

Core Idea
The Prophet set 'ushr rates based on effort, not actual costs; thus expenses are never deductible.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition establishes a clear principle: when calculating 'ushr on agricultural produce, one may not deduct costs for workers or animal feed. The proof is based on the Prophet's differentiation of rates for rain-irrigated versus artificially irrigated land, which shows that the rate itself accounts for hardship. Therefore, subsequent deductions are not allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The payment of 'ushr on agricultural produce. The ruling: it is wajib on the gross produce; no deduction for labor or animal expenses is allowed.
The act is the payment of 'ushr, not the cultivation itself.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The Prophet's ruling that the obligation varies according to the variation in effort (mu'nah). This refers to the hadith on different rates for rain-irrigated (full 'ushr) and irrigated with effort (half 'ushr).
The dalil is from Sunnah ahad, but it is well-known.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this hadith prove no deduction? Because the Prophet set the rate based on the type of irrigation (effort level), not on the actual expenses incurred. This implies that once the rate is fixed, no further expenses can be subtracted.
If expenses could be deducted, the rate would be adjusted per farm, which contradicts the fixed rate.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? The entire harvest is subject to 'ushr, regardless of costs. For example, 100 mann of wheat incurs 'ushr on the full 100 mann, even if 10 mann were spent on workers.
This ensures a straightforward calculation and prevents evasion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عشر سے اجرت عمال اور بیلوں کے خرچ کو منہا نہیں کیا جائے گا
قَالَ وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ أَخْرَجَتْهُ الْأَرْضُ مِمَّا فِيهِ الْعُشْرُ لَا يُحْتَسَبُ فِيهِ أَجْرُ الْعُمَّالِ وَ نَفَقَةُ الْبَقَرِ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ حَكَمَ بتَفَاوُتِ الواجب لتفاوتِ المُؤْنَةِ فَلَا مَعْنَى لِرَفْعِهَا۔ ترجمہ امام محمد نے کہا کہ ہر وہ چیز جس کو زمین سے نکالا اور اس میں عشر واجب ہے تو اس میں کام کرنے والوں کی اجرت اور بیلوں کا چارہ محسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مختلف مشقتوں کی وجہ سے مختلف واجبات کا حکم دیا ہے پس خرچہ محسوب کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جن زمینوں کی پیداوار میں عشر یا نصف عشر لیا جاتا ہے ان کی پیداوار میں کام کرنے والوں کی اجرت اور بیلوں کے کھانے دانے کا خرچہ محسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا مثلا پیداوار ایک سو من گندم ہے اور دس من کام کرنے والوں کو اجرت اور جانوروں کے کھانے والے پر چلا گیا تو اس دس من کو محسوب کر کے باقی نوے من میں عشر واجب نہ کیا جائے گا بلکہ پوری پیداوار یعنی ایک سو من میں عشر واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مختلف مؤنتوں اور خرچوں کی وجہ سے مختلف واجبات کا حکم دیا ہے لہذا خرچہ وغیرہ کو محسوب کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔
The expenses for workers and oxen will not be deducted from the 'ushr. He (Imam Muhammad) said: And everything that the earth produces from that on which 'ushr is due, the wages of workers and the feed of oxen are not reckoned in it, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, ruled that the obligation varies according to the variation in effort, so there is no meaning for its removal. Translation: Imam Muhammad said that for everything extracted from the earth on which 'ushr is obligatory, the wages of workers and the fodder of oxen are not counted, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, has commanded different obligations based on different degrees of hardship, so there is no meaning to counting expenses. Explanation: The issue is that in the produce of lands from which 'ushr or half-'ushr is taken, the wages of workers and the cost of feed for animals are not deducted. For example, if produce is one hundred manns of wheat and ten manns went to workers' wages and animal feed, then after deducting those ten manns, 'ushr is not imposed on the remaining ninety manns; rather, 'ushr is obligatory on the full produce, i.e., one hundred manns. Because the Prophet, peace be upon him, has commanded different obligations based on different expenses and costs, so there is no meaning to deducting expenses.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states clearly that when calculating 'ushr on agricultural produce, one must not deduct the costs incurred for labor (wages of workers) and animal upkeep (feed for oxen). The proof is that the Prophet legislated varying rates of 'ushr (full tenth for rain-irrigated, half-tenth for irrigated with effort) based on the level of exertion (mu'nah), not on actual expenses. Therefore, once the rate is set, further deductions are irrelevant. The example given: if a harvest yields 100 manns of wheat and 10 manns are spent on workers and oxen, 'ushr is still calculated on the entire 100 manns, not on 90. This prevents evasion and simplifies the calculation.

Key Terms
أجر العمال (ajr al-‘ummāl): Wages paid to workers who cultivate the land.
نفقة البقر (nafaqat al-baqar): Expenses for feeding oxen or other animals used in farming.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a farmer produces 200 manns of wheat and spends 20 manns on workers and oxen, on how much wheat is 'ushr calculated according to the Hanafi school?
A) 180 manns
B) 200 manns
C) 20 manns
D) 10 manns

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, 'ushr is wajib on the entire gross produce; no deduction for labor or animal expenses is permitted.

Double 'Ushr on Taghlibi for 'Ushr Land: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and ijma proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the 'ushr rate for a Taghlibi on 'ushr land, explain the ijma' proof, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding land purchased from a Muslim.

Core Idea
A Taghlibi pays double 'ushr by consensus, but Imam Muhammad exempts land bought from a Muslim—a rare intra-Hanafi exception.

In this lesson, we examine how much 'ushr a Taghlibi (a Christian Arab) pays on 'ushr land. The Hanafi school holds that double 'ushr is obligatory, based on the consensus of the Companions during 'Umar's caliphate. However, a notable intra-Hanafi dispute arises from Imam Muhammad's narration that if the Taghlibi buys the land from a Muslim, only one 'ushr is due. Understanding this dispute reveals how later Hanafis weighed different narrations and established the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the general rule: a Taghlibi on 'ushr land pays double 'ushr, regardless of how he acquired the land.
The ruling is wajib.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is ijma' of the Companions, specifically the consensus during 'Umar's caliphate that Banu Taghlib pay double what Muslims pay.
Ijma' is a qat'i source.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi exception
Imam Muhammad narrates that if a Taghlibi buys 'ushr land from a Muslim, only one 'ushr is due, because the duty (wazifa) does not change with ownership transfer.
This is a weak narration, not part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwayah position: double 'ushr in all cases. Imam Muhammad's exception is not relied upon for fatwa.
The commentary favors the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تغلمی کی عشری زمین میں کتنا عشر ہے
قَالَ تَغْلِيُّ لَهُ أَرْضُ عُشْرٍ فَعَلَيْهِ الْعُشْرُ مَضَاعَفًا عُرِفَ ذَلِكَ بِإِجْمَاعِ الصَّحَابَةِ رِضْوَانُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَعَنْ مـ أنَّ فِيْمَا اشْتَرَاهُ التَّعْلِبِيُّ مِنَ الْمُسْلِم عُشْرًا وَاحِدًا لأنَّ الوَظِيفَةَ عِندَهُ لَا تَتَغَيَّرُ بِتَغَيرِ الْمَالِكِ ترجمه امام محمد نے کہا کہ ایک تعلیمی کی عشری زمین ہے تو اس پر دو چند عشر واجب ہو گا یہ بات صحابہ کے اجماع سے معلوم ہوئی ہے۔ اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ تعلیمی نے مسلمانوں سے جو عشری زمین خریدی اس میں ایک ہی عشر ہے کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک مالک کے بدلنے سے حکم نہیں بدلتا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ تعلیمی کی عشری زمین میں عشر کا دو چند واجب ہوگا وہ زمین خواہ ابتداء سے تعلیمی کی ہو یا تعلیمی نے اس کو کسی مسلمان سے خریدا ہو۔ دلیل صحابہ رضوان اللہ تعالی علیم کا اجماع ہے کیونکہ عبد عمر میں اس پر اجماع ہو چکا ہے کہ مسلمانوں سے جو لیا جاتا ہے بنو تغلب سے اس کا دو چند لیا جائے گا پس چونکہ عشری زمین میں مسلمان سے ایک عشر لیا جاتا ہے تو تعلمی سے اس کا دو چند لیا جائے گا ۔ امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ تعلیمی نے اگر عشری زمین کسی مسلمان سے خریدی ہو تو اس میں ایک ہی عشر واجب ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک مالک کے بدلنے سے حکم تبدیل نہیں ہوتا پس جب یہ زمین مسلمان کی ملک میں تھی تو ایک عشر واجب تھا اور اب جبکہ تغلطی کی ملک میں آگئی تو اب بھی ایک ہی عشر واجب ہوگا۔
زمی نے تعلیمی سے زمین خریدی تو مذکورہ بالا مسئلہ کا حکم جاری ہوگا
فَإِنِ اشْتَرَاهَا مِنْهُ ذَمِّيُّ فَهِيَ عَلَى حَالِهَا عِنْدَهُمْ لِجَوَارِ التَّصْعِيفِ عَلَيْهِ فِى الْجُمْلَةِ كَمَا إِذَا مَرَّ عَلَى الْعَاشِرِ ترجمہ پھر اگر تعلیمی سے یہ زمین کسی ذمی نے خرید لی تو بالا اتفاق یہ اپنے حال پر رہے گی کیونکہ ذمی پر فی الجملہ دو چند کا وجوب ہوتا ہے جیسے کہ جب عاشر کے پاس سے گذرا ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عشری زمین کو کسی غیر تعلمی ذمی نے تعلیمی سے خرید لیا تو بالاتفاق اس غیر تعلیمی ذمی پر بھی عشر کا دو چند واجب
How much 'ushr is there on a Taghlibi's 'ushr land? He said: A Taghlibi, he has an 'ushr land, so upon him is double 'ushr; this is known by the consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. And from Muhammad that on what the Taghlibi buys from a Muslim, one 'ushr, because the duty in his view does not change with the change of owner. Translation: Imam Muhammad said that a Taghlibi has an 'ushr land, so upon him is double 'ushr; this is known from the consensus of the Companions. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that if a Taghlibi buys an 'ushr land from Muslims, there is only one 'ushr, because according to Imam Muhammad, the ruling does not change with the change of owner. Explanation: The issue is that double 'ushr is obligatory on a Taghlibi's 'ushr land, whether the land was originally his or he bought it from a Muslim. The proof is the consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, because consensus was reached during the time of Umar that what is taken from Muslims, double is taken from Banu Taghlib. So since from a Muslim on 'ushr land one 'ushr is taken, from a Taghlibi double is taken. It is narrated from Imam Muhammad that if a Taghlibi bought 'ushr land from a Muslim, then only one 'ushr is obligatory, because according to Imam Muhammad, the ruling does not change with the change of owner. When the land was owned by a Muslim, one 'ushr was obligatory, and now that it has come into the ownership of a Taghlibi, still only one 'ushr is obligatory. If a dhimmī buys the land from the Taghlibi, then the above ruling applies. He said: Then if a dhimmī buys it from him, it remains in its state according to them, because the doubling is permissible upon him in general, as when he passes by the collector. Translation: Then if a dhimmī buys this land from the Taghlibi, then by agreement it remains in its state, because the dhimmī is subject to doubling in general, like when he passes by the collector. Explanation: If a non-Taghlibi dhimmī buys an 'ushr land from a Taghlibi, then by consensus double 'ushr is also obligatory on that non-Taghlibi dhimmī.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about the 'ushr rate on 'ushr land when owned by a Taghlibi (a Christian Arab tribe). The matn states that a Taghlibi pays double 'ushr, based on the consensus of the Companions (ijma'). The commentary explains that this applies whether the land is originally owned by the Taghlibi or purchased from a Muslim. However, a narration from Imam Muhammad says that if the Taghlibi buys the land from a Muslim, only one 'ushr is due, because the legal obligation does not change with the transfer of ownership—the land's status remains as it was when owned by the Muslim. The passage then extends the ruling: if a dhimmī (a non-Taghlibi dhimmī) purchases the land from the Taghlibi, by consensus the dhimmī also pays double 'ushr, because dhimmīs are generally subject to double tolls when passing customs (like the tithe collector). This shows the heavy tax on non-Muslims in 'ushr lands.

Key Terms
تغلبي (Taghlibī): A member of the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib, who are treated differently in jizya and 'ushr.
مضاعف (muḍā‘af): Double, i.e., twice the normal rate of 'ushr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the proof for the ruling that a Taghlibi pays double 'ushr on 'ushr land?
A) Quran
B) Sunnah
C) Ijma' of Companions
D) Qiyas

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a Taghlibi pays double 'ushr on 'ushr land by ijma', and this applies even if he buys the land from a Muslim, despite Imam Muhammad's minority exception.

Expenses Not Deducted from 'Ushr on Produce
Ruling that labor and fodder costs are not deducted from total produce for 'ushr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that expenses are not deducted for 'ushr and explain the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Prophet tied 'ushr rates to effort, not net profit – expenses are irrelevant for the zakah share.

When you harvest your crop, you might think you should subtract your costs before paying 'ushr. But this lesson shows that the Hanafi school, following Imam Muhammad, rules otherwise. The obligation is on the total produce, not the profit. Let's see the reasoning and the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled? Imam Muhammad states that for any produce subject to 'ushr, the wages of workers and fodder of oxen are not deducted. The ruling is that 'ushr is obligatory on the total produce.
This is a clear ruling statement without dispute within the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the general practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who prescribed different obligations (e.g., 10% for rain-fed, 5% for irrigated) based on different difficulties.
The dalil is from Sunnah ahad, but its meaning is clear and accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove that expenses are not deducted? The Prophet varied the 'ushr rate based on the type of effort (irrigation), not on the amount of input costs. This indicates that the base for 'ushr is the total yield, and expenses are not a factor.
The differentiation is a fixed legal classification, not a sliding scale for costs.
4
Apply the ruling to an example
The text gives an example: if 100 mans of wheat is produced and 10 mans are spent on wages and fodder, 'ushr is due on the full 100 mans, not on 90 mans. Work through this arithmetic to confirm.
This concrete illustration anchors the abstract rule.
5
Note the uniqueness
This ruling is specific to agricultural zakah. In business zakah, expenses are handled differently; there, the obligation is on the net value of trade goods after one year, but operational costs are not deducted from the valuation. Here, the principle is absolute: no deduction.
Avoid conflating different types of zakah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ امام محمد نے کہا کہ ہر وہ چیز جس کو زمین سے نکالا اور اس میں عشر واجب ہے تو اس میں کام کرنے والوں کی اجرت اور بیلوں کا چارہ محسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مختلف مشقتوں کی وجہ سے مختلف واجبات کا حکم دیا ہے پس خرچہ محسوب کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جن زمینوں کی پیداوار میں عشر یا نصف عشر لیا جاتا ہے ان کی پیداوار میں کام کرنے والوں کی اجرت اور بیلوں کے کھانے دانے کا خرچہ محسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا مثلا پیداوار ایک سو من گندم ہے اور دس من کام کرنے والوں کو اجرت اور جانوروں کے کھانے والے پر چلا گیا تو اس دس من کو محسوب کر کے باقی نوے من میں عشر واجب نہ کیا جائے گا بلکہ پوری پیدا وار یعنی ایک سومن میں عشر واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مختلف مؤنتوں اور خرچوں کی وجہ سے مختلف واجبات کا حکم دیا ہے لہذا خرچہ وغیرہ کو محسوب کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔
Imam Muhammad said: Everything that is extracted from the land and upon which 'ushr is obligatory, the wages of the workers and the fodder of the oxen will not be deducted from it, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed different obligations due to different difficulties. So there is no meaning in deducting expenses. Explanation: The issue is that for lands whose produce is subject to 'ushr or half-'ushr, the wages of the workers and the cost of animal feed are not deducted. For example, if the produce is 100 mans of wheat, and 10 mans were spent on wages and animal feed, then that 10 mans will not be deducted and 'ushr will be obligatory on the full produce, i.e., 100 mans. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed different obligations based on different expenses, so there is no meaning in deducting expenses.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This is a ruling statement by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, from Zahir al-Riwayah, that when calculating 'ushr on agricultural produce, no deduction is made for labor wages or animal fodder. The proof is the Prophet's (peace be upon him) practice of prescribing different obligations based on the level of exertion involved in different types of wealth (e.g., 10% on rain-fed land, 5% on irrigated land). Since 'ushr is a religious obligation on the total produce, any expenses incurred in cultivation are irrelevant for the share due to Allah. The example clarifies that if 100 mans of wheat is produced, and 10 mans are spent on inputs, 'ushr is still calculated on the full 100 mans, not on the net 90 mans.

Key Terms
عشر (‘ushr): One-tenth of agricultural produce due as zakat on rain-fed land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Such expenses must be deducted before calculating 'ushr.
B) Such expenses are not deducted; 'ushr is on the total produce.
C) Only animal feed is deducted, not workers' wages.
D) It depends on whether the land is rain-fed or irrigated.

Key Takeaway
Expenses are never deducted from total produce for 'ushr; the obligation is on the full harvest, as established by the Prophet's differentiation of rates based on effort, not on input costs.

Double 'Ushr on Banu Taghlib's Land
Intra-Hanafi dispute on double 'ushr for Banu Taghlib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on double 'ushr for Banu Taghlib and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad regarding land purchased from a Muslim.

Core Idea
Banu Taghlib pay double 'ushr, established by ijma al-Sahaba, even if land was bought from a Muslim.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses the tax (ushr) on agricultural land owned by members of Banu Taghlib, a Christian Arab tribe. The main ruling, based on consensus of the Companions, imposes double the usual rate. However, a narration from Imam Muhammad introduces a nuance when the land was purchased from a Muslim. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh ijma against a qiyas-based principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act? A Taghlibi owns 'ushr land. What is the hukm? Double 'ushr is wajib.
The text states: 'A Taghlibi who has an 'ushr land is obligated to pay double 'ushr.'
2
Locate the primary proof
The proof is ijma of the Companions, particularly during 'Umar's caliphate. This is a strong source in Hanafi usul.
Ijma is a primary source of law after Quran and Sunnah.
3
Note the opposing view
Imam Muhammad narrates that if the Taghlibi bought the land from a Muslim, only single 'ushr is due.
This is a weaker narration (nawadir), but it represents a legitimate qiyas.
4
Understand the reasoning behind each position
The main view relies on the explicit ijma that Banu Taghlib pay double what Muslims pay. Muhammad's view relies on the principle that the land's function (wazifah) does not change with owner change.
This is a conflict between a specific textual proof (ijma) and a general qiyas.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is double 'ushr in all cases because ijma overrides qiyas in Hanafi usul.
The Hidayah author favors the consensus view as the stronger proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ تَغْلِيُّ لَهُ أَرْضُ عُشْرٍ فَعَلَيْهِ الْعُشْرُ مَضَاعَفًا عُرِفَ ذَلِكَ بِإِجْمَاعِ الصَّحَابَةِ رِضْوَانُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَعَنْ مـ أنَّ فِيْمَا اشْتَرَاهُ التَّعْلِبِيُّ مِنَ الْمُسلِم عُشْرًا وَاحِدًا لأنَّ الوَظِيفَةَ عِندَهُ لَا تَتَغَيَّرُ بِتَغَيرِ الْمَالِكِ
ترجمه امام محمد نے کہا کہ ایک تعلمی کی عشری زمین ہے تو اس پر دو چند عشر واجب ہو گا یہ بات صحابہ کے اجماع سے معلوم ہوئی ہے۔ اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ تعلیمی نے مسلمانوں سے جو عشری زمین خریدی اس میں ایک ہی عشر ہے کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک مالک کے بدلنے سے حکم نہیں بدلتا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ تعلیمی کی عشری زمین میں عشر کا دو چند واجب ہوگا وہ زمین خواہ ابتداء سے تعلیمی کی ہو یا تعلیمی نے اس کو کسی مسلمان سے خریدا ہو۔ دلیل صحابہ رضوان اللہ تعالی علیم کا اجماع ہے کیونکہ عبد عمر میں اس پر اجماع ہو چکا ہے کہ مسلمانوں سے جو لیا جاتا ہے بنو تغلب سے اس کا دو چند لیا جائے گا پس چونکہ عشری زمین میں مسلمان سے ایک عشر لیا جاتا ہے تو تعلمی سے اس کا دو چند لیا جائے گا ۔ امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ تعلیمی نے اگر عشری زمین کسی مسلمان سے خریدی ہو تو اس میں ایک ہی عشر واجب ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک مالک کے بدلنے سے حکم تبدیل نہیں ہوتا پس جب یہ زمین مسلمان کی ملک میں تھی تو ایک عشر واجب تھا اور اب جبکہ تغلطی کی ملک میں آگئی تو اب بھی ایک ہی عشر واجب ہوگا۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: A Taghlibi who has an 'ushr land is obligated to pay double 'ushr. That is established by the consensus of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them). And it is narrated from Muhammad that on what the Taghlibi buys from a Muslim, there is a single 'ushr, because in his view the function (wazifah) does not change with the change of owner. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: A Taghlibi has an 'ushr land, so double 'ushr is obligatory on him. This matter is known from the consensus of the Companions. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that if a Taghlibi purchases an 'ushr land from Muslims, then there is only a single 'ushr on it, because in Imam Muhammad's view the ruling does not change with the change of owner. Explanation: The issue is that on a Taghlibi's 'ushr land, double 'ushr is obligatory, whether the land was originally Taghlibi's or the Taghlibi purchased it from a Muslim. The proof is the consensus of the Companions, because during the caliphate of 'Umar, there was consensus that what is taken from Muslims is taken double from Banu Taghlib. Since from a Muslim on 'ushr land one 'ushr is taken, from a Taghlibi double will be taken. It is narrated from Imam Muhammad that if a Taghlibi purchased 'ushr land from a Muslim, then only one 'ushr is obligatory. Because in Imam Muhammad's view, the ruling does not change with the change of owner. So when this land was in the ownership of a Muslim, one 'ushr was obligatory, and now that it has come into the ownership of a Taghlibi, still only one 'ushr will be obligatory.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on Banu Taghlib (a Christian Arab tribe) who own 'ushr land. The main ruling, supported by the consensus of the Companions (specifically during 'Umar's caliphate), is that they must pay double the 'ushr that Muslims pay—i.e., 20% instead of 10%. The basis for this is a political/legal distinction: Banu Taghlib, though Christian, were treated as having a status between Muslims and dhimmis, and the double 'ushr served as a distinguishing tax. However, there is a narration from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that if the Taghlibi purchased the land from a Muslim, only a single 'ushr is due, because the land's function (wazifah) does not change simply because the owner changed. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, with the consensus view being the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
تغلمی (Taghlibi): A member of the Banu Taghlib, a Christian Arab tribe that was not forced to convert but had special tax rules.
تضعیف (tat‘if): Making something double; here, the double 'ushr on Banu Taghlib's land.
اجماع صحابہ (ijma‘ al-Sahabah): Consensus of the Companions of the Prophet, considered a binding proof in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A direct verse from the Quran.
B) A hadith from the Prophet.
C) The consensus of the Companions.
D) A ruling from the caliphs after the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Banu Taghlib must pay double 'ushr on their 'ushr land, regardless of how they acquired it, based on the binding consensus of the Companions.

Double ‘Ushr on Dhimmi Buying Taghlib’s Land
Ruling that double 'ushr remains on Taghlib's land when purchased by a dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on double 'ushr when a dhimmi purchases 'ushr land from a Taghlibi and explain the general principle that supports it.

Core Idea
Double 'ushr on Taghlib's land remains even when a dhimmi buys it, because dhimmis are generally subject to double customs.

In the Hanafi school, certain lands owned by Christians of Banu Taghlib are subject to double 'ushr. When a dhimmi purchases such land, one might wonder if the rate changes. This lesson clarifies that the double obligation remains by consensus, grounded in the general rule that dhimmis pay double customs in trade.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a dhimmi purchasing 'ushr land from a Taghlibi. The ruling is that double 'ushr remains obligatory on the dhimmi purchaser.
The ruling is by consensus of the Hanafi imams.
2
Understand the parties
The seller is a Taghlibi (a Christian from Banu Taghlib, whose land is subject to double 'ushr). The buyer is a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state).
The ruling might differ if the buyer were a Muslim.
3
Recognize the consensus
The text states that all scholars (i.e., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) agree that the land remains in its state of double 'ushr.
This is a rare case of unanimity within the Hanafi school.
4
Grasp the underlying principle
The reason given is that dhimmis are generally subject to double customs (tat‘if). For example, when a dhimmi passes a customs officer with trade goods, he pays double what a Muslim pays.
This principle is rooted in the social contract with dhimmis, not in the land itself.
5
Apply the principle
Since the dhimmi is already liable for double rates on trade, the same logic extends to the 'ushr on land purchased from Taghlib. Therefore, the double 'ushr remains.
No ikhtilaf exists on this point.

Source Text

Then if a dhimmi purchases it from him, it remains in its state according to them (all scholars), because double (tat‘if) is obligatory on him in general, just as when he passes by the customs officer. Explanation: The issue is that if a non-Taghlibi dhimmi purchases the 'ushr land from a Taghlibi, then by consensus double 'ushr becomes obligatory on this non-Taghlibi dhimmi as well, just as it was obligatory on the Taghlibi, because on a non-Taghlibi dhimmi double is generally obligatory. For example, if a dhimmi passes by a customs officer with trade goods, he must pay double the amount that a Muslim would pay.

Commentary
This is a clear ruling by agreement of the scholars (presumably Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad). When a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state) buys 'ushr land from a Banu Taghlib Christian, the double 'ushr obligation remains on the dhimmi purchaser. The reason given is that, in general, dhimmis are subject to double customs or taxes in trade (e.g., when passing a customs checkpoint, they pay double what a Muslim pays). So applying double 'ushr on the land is consistent with this principle. There is no dispute on this point; it is unanimous.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state who pays jizya and is protected.
تعلیمی (Taghlibi): A Christian from the Banu Taghlib tribe, whose land is subject to double 'ushr in the Hanafi school.

Double 'ushr on Taghlib's land remains unchanged when a dhimmi purchases it, due to the general rule imposing double customs on dhimmis.

Effect of Muslim Ownership or Conversion on Double ‘Ushr: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on double 'ushr continuity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on whether double 'ushr remains when a Muslim buys a Taghlibi's land or the owner converts, and apply the concept of wazifah to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Double 'ushr is a function of the land, not the owner — but the cause (Christianity) matters for some Hanafis.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute. While Abu Hanifa treats double 'ushr as a permanent burden on the land (like kharaj), Abu Yusuf sees it as connected to the owner's religion. Imam Muhammad offers a middle ground. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school balances textual analogy (qiyas) with legal maxims (wazifah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling scenario
The scenario: a Muslim buys 'ushr land from a Taghlibi (Christian Arab) or the Taghlibi converts to Islam. The question: does the double 'ushr (20%) remain or revert to single (10%)?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa: the double 'ushr remains in all cases because it has become a function (wazifah) of the land, like kharaj. The burden transfers with the land regardless of the owner's faith.
Key concept: wazifah — a fixed levy attached to the property itself.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and his dalil
Abu Yusuf: the double 'ushr reverts to single 'ushr because the cause that triggered the doubling (the owner's Christianity) is removed.
Cause-and-effect reasoning: the ruling follows the 'illah.
4
State Imam Muhammad's nuanced position
Imam Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa on the continuity of double 'ushr, but only if the doubling was original (asli) — i.e., the land already had double 'ushr from the beginning (e.g., inherited). If the doubling was new (hadith) — i.e., it arose only after a Taghlibi bought the land from a Muslim — then the double 'ushr is not realized in his view because the function does not change.
This distinction is based on the concept of wazifah not being created anew when the function was not established originally.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: a Muslim who buys such land pays 10% (Abu Yusuf/Muhammad-new) or 20% (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad-original). The mufta bihi (relied-upon view) is Abu Hanifa's, and it is reported that Muhammad agrees with him on original double.
The preferred view is continuity, but the nuance of original vs. new is important for fatwa.

وَكَذَا إِذَا اشْتَرَاهَا مِنْهُ مُسْلِمُ أَو أَسَلَمَ التَّغْلِى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ سَوَاء كَانَ التَّضْعِيفُ أَصْلِيًّا أو حَادِئًا لأنَّ التّضْعِيفَ صَارَ وَظِيفَةً لَهَا فَتَسْتَقِلُ إِلَى الْمُسْلِمِ بِمَا فِيْهَا كَالْخَرَاجِ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ يَعُودُ إلى عُشْرٍ وَاحِدٍ لِزَوَالِ الدَّاعِى إلى التَّصْعِيفِ قَالَ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ فِيْمَا صَحَّ عَنْهُ قَالَ اخْتَلَفَتِ النُّسُخُ فِي بَيَانِ قَوْلِهِ وَالْأَصَحُ أَنَّهُ مَعَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ فِي بَقَاءِ التَّضْعِيْفِ إِلَّا أَنَّ قَوْلَهُ لَايَتَاتَى إِلَّا فِي الْأَصْلِى لِأَنَّ التَّضْعِيفَ الْحَادِثَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ عِنْدَ العَدَمِ تُغَيَّرِ الْوَظِيفَةِ
ترجمہ اور اسی طرح اگر تعلمی سے اس زمین کو کسی مسلمان نے خریدا یا تعلمی مسلمان ہو گیا تو بھی ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ( دو چند ہوگا ) خواہ دو چند ہونا اصلی ہو یا حادث ہو کیونکہ دو چند ہی اس زمین کا وظیفہ ہو گیا ہے پس یہ زمین مسلمان کی طرف خراج وغیرہ اپنے تمام بار بوجھ کے ساتھ منتقل ہو جائے گی اور ابو یوسف نے کہا ہے کہ ایک عشر کی طرف لوٹے گی کیونکہ دو چند کی طرف جو امر باعث تھائی زائل ہوگی اور مسو کی کتب (الزکوۃ) میں کہا کہ صحیح روایت میں یہی قول امام محمد سے ثابت ہے۔ مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ امام محمد کے قول بیان کرنے میں نسخے مختلف ہیں اور اصبح یہ کہ امام محمد کا قول امام ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ ہے دو چند باقی رہنے میں مگر امام محمد کا قول نہیں حاصل ہو گا تضعیف اصلی میں کیونکہ تضعیف جو حادث ہو وہ امام محمد کے نزدیک متحقق نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ وظیفہ متغیر نہیں ہوتا۔
And likewise, if a Muslim buys it from him, or the Taghlibi becomes Muslim, according to Abu Hanifa (the double 'ushr remains) whether the doubling was original or new, because the doubling has become a function (wazifah) of the land, so it transfers to the Muslim with all its burdens, like kharaj. Abu Yusuf said: It reverts to a single 'ushr because the cause that led to doubling is removed. It is said in the book (al-Mabsut) that this is the statement of Muhammad as authentically reported from him. He (the author of Hidayah) said: The manuscripts differ concerning the statement of Muhammad, and the most correct is that he is with Abu Hanifa regarding the continuation of the doubling, except that his statement can only be realized in the original (double), because the new doubling cannot be realized in his view when the function does not change. Translation: And likewise, if a Muslim buys this land from a Taghlibi, or the Taghlibi becomes Muslim, then according to Abu Hanifa (double 'ushr will be obligatory) whether the doubling was original or new, because the doubling has become the function of this land. So this land will transfer to the Muslim with all its burdens like kharaj. Abu Yusuf said that it will revert to a single 'ushr because the cause for the doubling is removed. And in the book of zakat (al-Mabsut) it is said that this statement is authentically reported from Imam Muhammad. The author (of Hidayah) said that the manuscripts differ concerning the statement of Imam Muhammad, and the most correct is that his statement agrees with Abu Hanifa regarding the continuation of the doubling, except that his statement can only apply to the original doubling, because the new doubling cannot be realized in his view since the function does not change.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding what happens to the double 'ushr on Taghlib's land when the owner changes to a Muslim (either by purchase or conversion). Abu Hanifa holds that the double 'ushr remains attached to the land permanently, whether the land originally had double 'ushr (e.g., inherited from a Taghlibi father) or the double 'ushr was newly imposed when a Taghlibi bought from a Muslim. His reason: the double 'ushr has become a fixed function (wazifah) of the land itself, like kharaj (land tax) which transfers with the land regardless of the owner's faith. Abu Yusuf argues that the double 'ushr reverts to single 'ushr because the cause (the owner's Christianity) is removed. The author mentions that in al-Mabsut, Imam Muhammad's authentic position is stated to agree with Abu Yusuf (reverting to single). However, the author of Hidayah notes that manuscripts differ on Muhammad's view, and the more correct understanding is that Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa on the continuity of double 'ushr, but only in the case of original doubling. If the double 'ushr was newly imposed when the Taghlibi bought from a Muslim, Muhammad does not consider it valid because the function does not change in his view. So there are three nuanced positions: Abu Hanifa: double remains in all cases; Abu Yusuf: reverts to single; Muhammad: double remains only in original doubling, not new.

Key Terms
وظیفہ (wazifah): A fixed levy or function attached to a property; here, the double 'ushr becomes an inherent burden on the land.
تضعیف اصلی (tat‘if asli): Original doubling: when the land already had double 'ushr from the beginning (e.g., inherited from a Taghlibi).
تضعیف حادث (tat‘if hadith): New doubling: when the double 'ushr arose after a Taghlibi bought the land from a Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It reverts to single 'ushr.
B) The double 'ushr remains because it is now a function of the land.
C) The double 'ushr is cancelled entirely.
D) It depends on whether the Muslim converts the land.

Key Takeaway
The double 'ushr on Taghlibi land is tied to the land itself (wazifah) in Abu Hanifa's view, but the cause (Christianity) matters to Abu Yusuf, leading to a nuanced intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Double Ushr on Taghlibi Land: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on double ushr when taghlibi land passes to a Muslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on double ushr for taghlibi land transferred to a Muslim and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The land's tax burden is a function (wazifah) of the land, not the owner's faith.

When a Muslim purchases land from a taghlibi Christian or the taghlibi converts, does the double ushr continue? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute. Abu Hanifa holds that it continues, while Abu Yusuf argues it reverts to single ushr. Imam Muhammad's position is nuanced. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi principle that land taxes are attached to the land itself, not the owner's personal status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage considers two cases: a Muslim buys land from a taghlibi, or the taghlibi owner converts to Islam. In both, the question is whether the double ushr (two-tenths) remains.
The taghlibi are Christians from Banu Taghlib who were allowed to keep their land with double ushr.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that double ushr remains in both scenarios, whether the doubling was original (inherited) or incidental (from a previous Muslim owner). His proof: the doubling has become an established function (wazifah) of the land, so it transfers like kharaj does.
The analogy to kharaj is key: kharaj on a kharaji land does not change when the owner becomes Muslim.
3
State Abu Yusuf's ruling and reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that the double ushr reverts to single ushr because the cause (sabab) for doubling—the taghlibi's unbelief—has been removed.
He views the doubling as contingent on the owner's status, not inherent to the land.
4
Analyze Muhammad's position as reconciled by al-Hidayah
The author notes that manuscripts differ on Muhammad's view. The most correct (al-asahh) is that Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa on the continuation of doubling, but only for original doubling; incidental doubling cannot occur because the function of the land (single ushr) does not change when the owner changes.
This means if a taghlibi bought land from a Muslim that had only single ushr, it remains single even after the purchase.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as stated in al-Hidayah: 'al-asahhu annahu ma'a Abi Hanifah'. Thus, in practice, double ushr continues regardless of whether the doubling was original or incidental.
For fatwa, one follows Abu Hanifa's view.

وَكَذَا إِذَا اشْتَرَاهَا مِنْهُ مُسْلِمُ أَو أَسَلَمَ التَّغْلِى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ سَوَاء كَانَ التَّضْعِيفُ أَصْلِيًّا أو حَادِئًا لأنَّ التّضْعِيفَ صَارَ وَظِيفَةً لَهَا فَتَسْتَقِلُ إِلَى الْمُسْلِمِ بِمَا فِيْهَا كَالْخَرَاجِ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ يَعُودُ إلى عُشْرٍ وَاحِدٍ لِزَوَالِ الدَّاعِى إلى التَّصْعِيفِ قَالَ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ فِيْمَا صَحَ عَنْهُ قَالَ اخْتَلَفَتِ النُّسُخُ فِي بَيَانِ قَوْلِه وَالْأَصَحُ أَنَّهُ مَعَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ فِي بَقَاءِ التَّضْعِيْفِ إِلَّا أَنَّ قَوْلَهُ لَايَتَاتَى إِلَّا فِي الْأَصْلِى لِأَنَّ التَّضْعِيفَ الْحَادِثَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ عِنْدَ العَدَمِ تُغَيَّرِ الوَظِيفَةِ
And likewise, if a Muslim buys it from him (the taghlibi) or the taghlibi becomes Muslim, according to Abu Hanifa (the double ushr remains) whether the doubling is original or incidental, because the doubling has become an established function for it (the land), so it transfers to the Muslim with all its burdens like kharaj. Abu Yusuf said: It returns to a single ushr due to the removal of the cause for doubling. He (the author) said in the book: And that is the saying of Muhammad in what is authenticated from him. He said: The manuscripts differ in explaining his saying, and the most correct is that he is with Abu Hanifa in the continuation of the doubling, except that his saying only applies to the original doubling, because incidental doubling cannot be actualized when the function changes due to non-existence.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning land originally belonging to a taghlibi (a Christian from Banu Taghlib) that either is purchased by a Muslim or whose owner converts to Islam. The question is whether the tax remains double ushr (two-tenths) or reverts to standard ushr (one-tenth). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the double ushr persists in both scenarios—whether the doubling was originally established (e.g., inherited) or incidental (e.g., purchased from a Muslim who had only single ushr). His reasoning is that the doubling has become a binding function (wazifah) of the land itself, akin to kharaj on a kharaji land; thus, when the land transfers to a Muslim, it carries all its existing obligations. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the double ushr ceases and only single ushr is due because the cause (sabab) for doubling—the taghlibi's unbelief—has been removed. The author of al-Hidayah notes that in al-Mabsut, the authenticated position of Imam Muhammad is actually in agreement with Abu Hanifa regarding the continuation of doubling, but only for original doubling; incidental doubling cannot occur in his view because the function of the land (single ushr) does not change when the owner changes. This passage illustrates how the Hanafi school uses the concept of 'wazifah' (established burden) to determine tax obligations regardless of the owner's faith.

Key Terms
تضعیف (tad'if): Doubling of the ushr tax, meaning two-tenths instead of one-tenth.
وظیفہ (wazifah): An established fixed duty or burden attached to the land, such as ushr or kharaj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muslim purchases land from a taghlibi Christian. According to Abu Hanifa, what tax is due on this land?
A) Single ushr (one-tenth)
B) Double ushr (two-tenths)
C) Kharaj
D) No tax for a Muslim owner

Key Takeaway
Double ushr on taghlibi land remains when a Muslim acquires it because the tax is a function of the land, not the owner's faith.

Tax on Land Sold by Muslim to Dhimmi: Three Hanafi Views
Intra-Hanafi dispute on land tax change upon sale to dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) regarding the tax due when a Muslim sells ushri land to a non-taghlibi dhimmi, and explain the reasoning (talil) behind each.

Core Idea
A dhimmi buying Muslim land may owe kharaj, double ushr, or single ushr — Hanafi imams differ on whether the tax follows the owner or the land.

Imagine a Muslim farmer sells his tithe-paying (ushri) land to a local non-Muslim protected subject (dhimmi) who is not from Banu Taghlib. What tax does the buyer now owe? The Hanafi school does not have a single answer: the three founding imams each derived different rulings based on different legal principles. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and shows how the same facts can lead to multiple valid conclusions within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Map the Scenario
Identify the key elements: seller (Muslim), buyer (non-taghlibi dhimmi), land (ushri). What is the legal issue? The tax due on the land after ownership changes hands.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa says kharaj is due. His reasoning: kharaj is more befitting to the state of a disbeliever (kafir). The tax changes from ushr to kharaj because the owner is now a dhimmi.
Kharaj is a land tax considered punitive and is imposed on non-Muslims.
3
State Abu Yusuf's Position
Abu Yusuf says double ushr (20%) is due, but the proceeds are spent in the channels of kharaj. His reasoning: analogy to a taghlibi Christian, who pays double ushr; changing to kharaj entirely is more difficult, so doubling is the easier adjustment.
Note the practical difference: double ushr is 20% of produce, while kharaj is a fixed annual amount.
4
State Muhammad's Position
Muhammad says the land remains ushri (single ushr, 10%). His reasoning: ushr has become a fixed burden (ma'unah) on the land, just like kharaj on kharaji land – it does not change when ownership transfers. He then notes two narrations on disbursement: one says spent in zakat channels, another in kharaj channels.
Muhammad's view ties the tax to the land's character, not the owner's status.
5
Summarize the Practical Consequence
The dhimmi pays different amounts: kharaj (varies by land value), double ushr (20%), or single ushr (10%). The proceeds go to different state funds: general treasury for kharaj, zakat recipients for ushr (per one narration). Later Hanafi practice generally follows Abu Hanifa.
The ikhtilaf shows the richness of Hanafi ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الْأَرْضُ لِمُسْلِمِ بَاعَهَا مِنْ نَصْرَانِى يُرِيدُ بِهِ دَمِيًّا غَيْر نَغْلِي وَقَبَصَهَا فَعَلَيْهِ الْخَرَاجُ عِند أبي حنيفة لأنَّه اليقُ بِحَالِ الْكَافِرِ وَعِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ عَلَيْهِ الْعُشْرَ مُضَاعَفًا وَيُصْرَفُ مَصَارِفُ الخَراج اعتبارًا بِالتَّعْلِي وَهَذَا أَهْوَنُ مِنَ التَبْدِيلِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ هِيَ عُشْرِيَّةٌ عَلَى حَالِهَا لِأَنَّهُ صَارَ مَوْنَةٌ لَهَا فَلَا تُتَبَدلُ كَالْخَرَاحِ ثُمَّ فِي رِوَايَةٍ يُصْرَفُ مَصَارِفَ الصَّدَقَاتِ وَ فِي رِوَايَةٍ مَصَارِفُ الْحَرَاج
And if the land belonged to a Muslim, he sold it to a Christian, meaning a dhimmi other than a taghlibi, and he took possession of it, then kharaj is due upon him according to Abu Hanifa because it is more befitting to the state of a disbeliever. According to Abu Yusuf, double ushr is due upon him, and it is spent in the channels of kharaj, by analogy to the taghlibi, and this is easier than replacement. According to Muhammad, it is ushri land as it was, because ushr has become a burden for it, so it does not change like kharaj. Then in one narration it is spent in the channels of charity (zakat), and in another narration in the channels of kharaj.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage discusses the tax obligation when a Muslim sells his ushri (tithe-paying) land to a non-taghlibi dhimmi (a protected non-Muslim subject who is not from Banu Taghlib). Imam Abu Hanifa rules that kharaj (land tax) becomes due on the dhimmi buyer, reasoning that kharaj is more appropriate for a disbeliever, as it contains an element of punishment. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that double ushr (two-tenths) is due, analogizing this dhimmi to a taghlibi, but the proceeds are spent in the same channels as kharaj (e.g., public works, defense). He considers doubling the ushr easier than completely changing the tax type (from ushr to kharaj). Imam Muhammad maintains that the land remains ushri (single ushr) because ushr has become a fixed burden (ma'unah) on the land, just as kharaj is fixed on kharaji land and does not change when ownership transfers. He then notes two narrations regarding the disbursement of the collected ushr: one says it is spent in the channels of zakat (charity), another in the channels of kharaj. This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf shows the different methodologies: Abu Hanifa prioritizes the status of the owner (kafir deserves kharaj), Abu Yusuf uses qiyas on taghlibi doubling, and Muhammad emphasizes the land's fixed function (wazifah).

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): A land tax imposed on non-Muslims (and sometimes Muslims) on kharaji land, distinct from ushr.
مونه (ma'unah): A fixed burden or expense attached to the land, synonymous with wazifah in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, what tax is due on a non-taghlibi dhimmi who buys ushri land from a Muslim?
A) Kharaj
B) Double ushr
C) Single ushr
D) No tax

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a Muslim sells ushri land to a dhimmi, the tax due may change or remain, reflecting different ways of balancing the nature of the land with the status of the owner.

Tax Status of 'Ushri Land Sold to a Dhimmi: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on land tax classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the tax status of 'ushri land sold to a dhimmi and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) of each imam.

Core Idea
When a dhimmi buys 'ushri land, Abu Hanifa imposes kharaj, Abu Yusuf doubles the 'ushr, and Muhammad keeps the single 'ushr—each based on a different legal logic.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the tax classification of 'ushri agricultural land when sold to a non-Muslim dhimmi. The three founding imams each provide a distinct ruling, illustrating how different principles (punitive suitability, analogy, and stability of fixed levies) lead to differing conclusions. Understanding this dispute enhances your ability to analyze how the Hanafi school accommodates internal diversity of opinion and how practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf) flow from each position.

Guided Path
1
State the case
Identify the scenario: a Muslim sells his 'ushri land to a dhimmi (non-Taghlibi). The dhimmi takes possession. The question is what tax is due on the land's produce.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that kharaj becomes wajib. His proof: kharaj contains a punitive element (meaning of 'uqubah), which is more suitable for a disbeliever's state. Since the owner is a kafir, kharaj is imposed.
His reasoning is based on the nature of the taxpayer, not the land's history.
3
Present Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf rules that doubled 'ushr (two-tenths) is wajib, but disbursed in the ways of kharaj. He analogizes (qiyas) the non-Taghlibi dhimmi to Banu Taghlib, who pay doubled 'ushr. He argues that doubling the 'ushr is a change in description (taghyir fi al-wasf), which is easier than substitution (tabdil) of changing to kharaj entirely.
The qiyas is based on the commonality of being a dhimmi subject to a punitive levy.
4
Present Muhammad al-Shaybani's position and proof
Imam Muhammad maintains the land remains 'ushri with single 'ushr. His proof: 'ushr has become the fixed burden (mu'nah) of the land, and the fixed levy does not change with change of owner. Just as kharaj land remains kharaji when sold to a Muslim, here 'ushri land remains 'ushri. He has two narrations on disbursement: one says it goes to the recipients of zakat, the other to kharaj funds.
His reasoning emphasizes the stability of the land's tax classification based on its original designation.
5
Compare the positions and note the practical differences
The three positions differ in the amount of tax (kharaj vs. doubled 'ushr vs. single 'ushr) and its disbursement. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is what the dhimmi farmer actually pays and where the state allocates the revenue.
No clear tarjih is given in this passage; later Hanafi works may prefer one.

عشر واجب ہوتا ہے اس طرح غیر تعلیمی ذمیوں پر بھی دو چند عشر واجب ہوگا البتہ اس کا مصرف وہی ہوگا جو خراج کا مصرف ہے امام ابو یوسف کہتے ہیں کہ عشر کو دو چند کرنا بہ نسبت تبدیل کر دینے کے آسان ہے یعنی عشر کو دو چند کرنا وصف میں تغیر کرنا ہے اور بجائے عشر کے خراج واجب کرنا تبدیل کرانا ہے اور تغیر فی الوصف آسان ہے بہ نسبت تبدیل کرنے کے اس لئے عشر کا دو چند لازم کیا گیا۔ اور امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عشر اس زمین کا مقررہ بار ہے یعنی اس زمین میں پہلے سے عشر مقرر ہے لہذا اب بھی عشر رہے گا کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک مالک کے بدلنے سے مقررہ وظیفہ نہیں بدلتا لہذا یہ زمین جب مسلمان کے پاس تھی تو اس پر عشر واجب تھا اور جب کافر کے پاس آئی تو بھی اس پر عشر واجب ہوگا۔ اس میں کوئی تبدیلی نہیں آئے گی جیسے کافر کی زمین پر خراج واجب ہوتا ہے اب اگر یہ زمین مسلمان کے پاس آگئی تو بھی اس پر خراج واجب ہوگا۔ پھر اس کے مصرف کے بارے میں امام محمد سے دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ اس کا مصرف مصارف زکوۃ ہیں۔ دوم یہ کہ اس کا مصرف مصارف خراج ہیں۔
And if the land belongs to a Muslim, he sold it to a Christian intending a dhimmi other than Taghlibi, and he took possession, then upon him is kharaj according to Abu Hanifa because it is more suitable for the state of the disbeliever. According to Abu Yusuf, upon him is doubled 'ushr, and it is spent in the ways of kharaj, by analogy to the Taghlibi, and this is easier than substitution. According to Muhammad, it remains 'ushri as it was because it has become an expense for it, so it does not change like kharaj. Then in one narration it is spent in the ways of sadaqat, and in one narration the ways of kharaj. [Translation of Urdu: explanation of the issue and the arguments of each imam.]
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the tax status of 'ushri land sold by a Muslim to a non-Taghlibi dhimmi. The author follows the order of the matn, then provides Urdu commentary. Abu Hanifa holds that kharaj becomes due because it is more suitable for the condition of a disbeliever, kharaj having punitive elements. Abu Yusuf analogizes to Banu Taghlib, who pay doubled 'ushr, and he rules that this dhimmi also pays doubled 'ushr but disbursed as kharaj, arguing that changing the description (doubling) is easier than substitution (changing to kharaj). Imam Muhammad maintains the land remains 'ushri with single 'ushr, because the fixed levy (wazifah) does not change with the owner, just as kharaj land remains kharaji when sold to a Muslim. Muhammad has two narrations on disbursement: one says it goes to the recipients of zakat, the other to the recipients of kharaj. The commentary explains the reasoning of each imam in detail.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on non-Muslim owners of conquered lands, considered a punitive levy.
عشر ('ushr): The tithe payable on agricultural produce from 'ushri land, usually one-tenth or one-twentieth.
تضعیف (taḍ‘īf): Doubling; here refers to doubling the 'ushr (two-tenths) on Banu Taghlib and analogously on other dhimmis.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here Abu Yusuf uses qiyas to extend the Taghlib ruling to non-Taghlibi dhimmis.
مؤنہ (mu'nah): Burden, expense; in the text, 'ushr is described as the mu'nah (fixed burden) of the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Kharaj, disbursed as kharaj
B) Doubled 'ushr, disbursed as kharaj
C) Single 'ushr, disbursed as zakat
D) Doubled 'ushr, disbursed as zakat

Key Takeaway
The dispute over 'ushri land sold to a dhimmi illustrates how three Hanafi imams derived different rulings from the principles of punitive suitability, analogical reasoning, and stability of fixed levies, with no single position definitively preferred in this passage.

The Tax on an Orchard Converted from Dar Khittah: Water Source Determines the Levy
Ruling on tax liability change due to irrigation method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for the tax due (ʿushr or kharāj) when a Muslim converts a dār khittah into an orchard, and explain the ʿilla (effective cause) based on the water source.

Core Idea
The tax on an orchard follows the water source: ʿushr for ʿushr water, kharāj for kharāj water.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Imām Muḥammad al-Shaybānī about land originally allocated as a dwelling in conquered territory (dār khittah). When the owner converts it into an orchard, the tax liability is not fixed by the land’s original status but depends on how the orchard is irrigated. Understanding this ruling reveals the Ḥanafī method of linking legal consequences to practical realities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is converting a dār khittah (conquered land allocated to a Muslim) into an orchard. The ruling is that the owner must pay either ʿushr or kharaj, depending on the irrigation method.
This is not about the original land classification; the ruling is conditional.
2
State the condition
The water source is the decisive factor. If watered with ʿushr water (rain, well, etc.), ʿushr is due. If watered with kharaj water (state-maintained canals), kharaj is due.
The passage explicitly contrasts the two water types.
3
Recognize the dalīl (proof)
Imām Muḥammad gives the reason: 'because the expense in such matters revolves around the water' (al-mūnah tadūru maʿa al-māʾ). This is a rational principle (qiyās) linking tax to irrigation cost.
This is a talīl (causation) argument, not a direct text.
4
Understand the ʿilla (effective cause)
The ʿilla is the type of water source, which determines the nature of the land's maintenance and productivity. ʿUshr water implies private cost, kharaj water implies state investment.
This ʿilla can be overridden by istiḥsān in other cases, but here it governs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَتْ لِمُسْلِمٍ دَارُ خِطَّةٍ فَجَعَلَهَا بُسْتَانًا فَعَلَيْهِ الْعُشْرُ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا سَقَاهُ بِمَاءِ الْعُشْرِ أُمَّا إِذَا كَانَتْ تَسْقَى بِمَاءِ الْحَرَاجِ فَفِيهَا الْحَرَاجُ لأنَّ الْمَوْنَة فِى مِثْلِ هَذَا تَدُورُ مَعَ الْمَاءِ
ترجمه امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کسی مسلمان کے لئے کوئی گھر مختط کر دیا ہو پھر مسلمان نے اس کو باغ بنالیا تو اس پر عشر واجب ہوگا یعنی جب اس کو عشری پانی سے سینچا ہو اور اگر اس کو خراجی پانی سے سینچا ہو تو اس میں خراج واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ اس جیسی زمین میں خرچہ پانی کے ساتھ گھومتا ہے۔
He (Muhammad) said: And if a Muslim has a house in a conquered land (dar khittah) and he makes it an orchard, then upon him is 'ushr. Its meaning: when he waters it with 'ushr water. As for when it is watered with kharaj water, then upon it is kharaj, because the expense in such matters revolves around the water. [Translation of Urdu: Imam Muhammad said: if a Muslim's house allocated in conquered land is turned into an orchard, 'ushr is due if watered by 'ushr water; if watered by kharaj water, kharaj is due, because the cost in such land depends on the water.]
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling stated by Imam Muhammad regarding land that was originally a 'dar khittah' – a house plot given to Muslims in a conquered territory. If the owner converts it into an orchard, the tax liability depends on the water source used for irrigation. If the water is from an 'ushr water source (e.g., rain or well), the produce is subject to 'ushr (tithe). If the water is from a kharaj water source (e.g., a canal maintained by the state with kharaj revenues), then kharaj is due. The underlying principle, as stated, is that the 'expense' (maintenance cost) is tied to the water source. This is a rule of istihsan or practicality: the tax follows the irrigation method because it indicates the nature of the land's productivity and resource usage.

Key Terms
دار خطۃ (dār khittah): A house or plot in a conquered territory allocated to Muslims by the imam for habitation.
ماء العشر (mā’ al-‘ushr): Water from sources not associated with kharaj, such as rain, wells, or streams not maintained by state kharaj funds.
ماء الخراج (mā’ al-kharāj): Water from canals or sources maintained using kharaj revenues, typically requiring the payment of kharaj on the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a Muslim waters his orchard from a well that he dug himself, what tax is due?
A) 'Ushr
B) Kharaj
C) No tax
D) Both

Key Takeaway
The tax on an orchard converted from dār khittah follows the water source: ‘ushr for ‘ushr water, kharāj for kharāj water.

Dar Khittah to Garden: 'Ushr or Kharaj Follows Water
Ruling on land converted from residential to agricultural use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a dar khittah converted to a garden and identify which tax applies based on the water source.

Core Idea
The tax on a converted dar khittah garden depends entirely on the water source: 'ushr for 'ushri water, kharaj for kharaji water.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a Muslim who receives a dar khittah (tax-free residential plot) in conquered land decides to turn it into a garden. What tax obligations arise? The ruling hinges on the water used for irrigation, not the land itself — a clear demonstration of the Hanafi principle that financial liability follows the source of expense.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial status
Start with a Muslim who owns a dar khittah (tax-free residential plot). The act is converting it into a garden.
Dar khittah is a specific type of land grant; not all homes are dar khittah.
2
State the ruling
Upon conversion, the land becomes liable for tax. The type depends on the water source used for irrigation.
3
Apply the water condition
If watered with 'ushri water (rain, wells, springs) → 'ushr. If watered with kharaji water (canals paying kharaj) → kharaj.
'Ushri water is free; kharaji water is from tax-paying sources.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The expense (tax) revolves with the water because water is the main cost in cultivation. This provides the legal rationale.
The phrase 'al-ma'unatu taduru ma'a al-ma' is a key Hanafi maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ: وَإِذَا كَانَتْ لِمُسْلِمٍ دَارُ خِطَّةٍ فَجَعَلَهَا بُسْتَانًا فَعَلَيْهِ الْعُشْرُ. مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا سَقَاهُ بِمَاءِ الْعُشْرِ. فَأَمَّا إِذَا كَانَتْ تَسْقَى بِمَاءِ الْخَرَاجِ فَفِيهَا الْخَرَاجُ. لِأَنَّ الْمَئُونَةَ فِي مِثْلِ هَذَا تَدُورُ مَعَ الْمَاءِ.
He said: When a Muslim has a dar khittah and makes it a garden, then upon him is the 'ushr. Its meaning is when he waters it with 'ushri water. As for when it is watered with kharaji water, then upon it is the kharaj. Because the expense in such a case revolves with the water.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage explains the rule for a Muslim who receives a designated plot of land (dar khittah) in a conquered territory, which is tax-free as long as it remains a residence. If he converts it into a garden, he becomes liable. The liability type depends on the water source: if watered with 'ushri water (rain, wells, etc.), he pays 'ushr (tithe); if with kharaji water (canals dug by non-Muslims, etc.), he pays kharaj. The principle is that the expense (tax) follows the water because water is the main cost factor in cultivation. This shows the Hanafi link between irrigation and land taxation.

Key Terms
دار خطة (dar khittah): A plot of land in a conquered territory assigned by the Imam to a Muslim as a residence, initially tax-free.
ماء العشر (ma' al-'ushr): Water that is free for public use, such as rainwater, well water, spring water, and major rivers not controlled by authorities.
ماء الخراج (ma' al-kharaj): Water from canals or systems that are maintained by state authorities and are themselves subject to kharaj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'Ushr
B) Kharaj
C) Nothing
D) Half 'ushr, half kharaj

Key Takeaway
The tax on a dar khittah converted to a garden follows the water source: 'ushr for 'ushri water, kharaj for kharaji water.

Tax on a Majusi's Property: Kharaj Over 'Ushr
Ruling on Majusi's tax liability with proof from 'Umar's precedent and reasoning on qurbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a Majusi's house and garden tax, explain why kharaj takes precedence over 'ushr, and identify the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on the rate.

Core Idea
A Majusi pays kharaj on his garden, not 'ushr, because 'ushr is an act of worship.

This lesson examines a nuanced taxation rule from the Hanafi school regarding a Majusi's (Zoroastrian) property. You will learn how the school distinguishes between a residence and a garden, and why even when land is watered by 'ushri water, kharaj is imposed instead of 'ushr. The passage also reveals an internal dispute between the two Sahibayn on the hypothetical 'ushr rate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the owner and property types
The subject is a Majusi (Zoroastrian). He has a house and a garden. Determine the tax rule for each.
The house is exempt based on Caliph 'Umar's policy.
2
Extract the ruling for the garden
If he converts the house into a garden, he must pay kharaj. Note that this applies even if irrigated with 'ushri water.
This is the central ruling.
3
Analyze the reason for kharaj over 'ushr
The text says 'ushr contains the meaning of qurbah (devotion), so it cannot be imposed on a non-Muslim. Kharaj is a punishment suitable for his state.
This is a proof based on the nature of the tax.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi analogy
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that by analogy, 'ushr would be due if applied, but they disagree on the rate: Muhammad says one 'ushr, Abu Yusuf says two.
This is a theoretical dispute; in practice kharaj applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمَجُوسِيِّ فِي دَارِهِ شَيْءٌ لِأَنَّ عُمَرَ جَعَلَ الْمَسَاكِنَ عَفْوًا. وَإِنْ جَعَلَهَا بُسْتَانًا فَعَلَيْهِ الْخَرَاجُ. وَإِنْ سَقَاهَا بِمَاءِ الْعُشْرِ لِتَعَذُّرِ إِيجَابِ الْعُشْرِ إِذْ فِيهِ مَعْنَى الْقُرْبَةِ فَتَعَيَّنَ الْخَرَاجُ. وَهُوَ عُقُوبَةٌ تَلِيقُ بِحَالِهِ. وَعَلَى قِيَاسِ قَوْلِهِمَا يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ فِي الْمَاءِ الْعُشْرِيِّ إِلَّا أَنَّ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ عُشْرًا وَاحِدًا وَعِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ عُشْرَانِ.
There is nothing upon the Majusi in his house because 'Umar made the residences exempt. And if he makes it a garden, then upon him is the kharaj. And if he waters it with 'ushri water, because it is difficult to impose 'ushr since it contains the meaning of devotion, so kharaj is determined. And it is a punishment suitable for his condition. And according to the analogy of their (the two Sahibayn's) statement, 'ushr would be obligatory in 'ushri water, except that according to Muhammad it is one 'ushr, and according to Abu Yusuf two 'ushrs.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage covers the tax liability of a Majusi (fire worshipper) on his property. Following the precedent of Caliph 'Umar, a Majusi's residence is tax-free ('afw). If he converts his house into a garden, he must pay kharaj, even if he waters it with 'ushri water. The reason is that 'ushr is an act of worship (qurbah) and cannot be imposed on a non-Muslim; instead, kharaj is levied as a punitive but just tax suitable for his status. The passage also notes that according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) by analogy, 'ushr would normally be due on 'ushri water, but in this case it is replaced by kharaj. It then mentions a dispute between the two: Imam Muhammad says one 'ushr (10%), while Abu Yusuf says two 'ushrs (20%) for the Majusi's garden. This shows the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on the rate for a non-Muslim's agricultural produce.

Key Terms
مجوسي (majusi): A Zoroastrian (fire worshipper), considered in Hanafi law as akin to People of the Book for taxation but not for marriage or slaughter.
عفو ('afw): Exempt from tax; here applied to residential property of non-Muslims as per 'Umar's policy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a Majusi pay kharaj on his garden even if watered with 'ushri water?
A) Because 'ushr water is not available to him.
B) Because 'ushr is an act of worship and cannot be imposed on a non-Muslim.
C) Because 'Umar ordered kharaj on all Majusi lands.
D) Because the garden is in a kharaji region.

Key Takeaway
A Majusi's garden is subject to kharaj, not 'ushr, because 'ushr is a devotional obligation unsuitable for a non-Muslim.
