Abrogation of Mu'allafatu al-Qulub as a Zakat Recipient
Listing zakat categories and proving abrogation of one

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Mu'allafatu al-Qulub and explain the ijma sukuti proof that abrogates this category.

Core Idea
Mu'allafatu al-Qulub is abrogated as a zakat recipient by the tacit consensus of the Companions.

The eight categories of zakat recipients are derived from Quran 9:60. The Hanafi school holds that one category, Mu'allafatu al-Qulub (those whose hearts are to be reconciled), is no longer valid after the death of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). This lesson unpacks the historical incident and the legal proof that established this abrogation, helping you understand how later rulings can modify earlier practices based on consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that Mu'allafatu al-Qulub is abrogated as a category for zakat distribution after the Prophet's death. Recognize that this is the Hanafi position.
2
Classify the three types of Mu'allafatu al-Qulub
The passage mentions three types: disbelievers hoped to convert, disbelievers feared for harm, and weak Muslims needing encouragement. Understand why each type was relevant in the Prophet's time.
3
Examine the historical incident
Read the story of 'Uyaynah and al-Aqra' coming to Abu Bakr, and then to Umar who tore up the decree, saying Islam is now dominant. Note that Abu Bakr concurred.
4
Recognize the ijma sukuti
The silence of the other Companions after Umar's action and Abu Bakr's approval constitutes a tacit consensus (ijma sukuti). In Hanafi usul, this is a binding proof.
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, the Hanafi school rules that the category of Mu'allafatu al-Qulub is no longer a valid recipient of zakat. Giving zakat under this category is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكوة
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
(۴) مؤلفة القلوب (جن کے اسلام لانے کی امید ہو یا اسلام میں کمزور ہوں۔ (۵) رقاب (یعنی غلاموں کا بدل کتابت ادا کر کے آزادی دلائی جائے یا خرید کر آزاد کئے جائیں یا اسیروں کا فدیہ دیکر رہا کرائے جائیں۔
(1) غار میں (جن پر کوئی حادثہ پڑا اور مقروض ہو گئے یا کسی ضمانت وغیرہ کے بارے میں دب گئے )۔ (۷) فی سبیل اللہ (جہاد وغیرہ میں جانے والوں کی اعانت کی جائے )۔
(۸) ابن السبیل مسافر جو حالت سفر میں مالک نصاب نہ ہو گو مکان پر دولت رکھتا ہو ) ۔ (مرشد تھانوی) صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ان آٹھ قسموں سے ایک قسم مؤلفۃ القلوب ساقط ہو گئی یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی وفات کے بعد یہ قسم نہیں رہی عنایہ میں ہے کہ مؤلفتہ القلوب کی تین قسمیں تھیں (۱) وہ کفار جن کو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اس واسطے عطا کرتے کہ ان کے دلوں کو اس حقیر ما یہ دنیاوی سے اسلام کی طرف لائیں ۔ (۲) وہ کفار جن کو اس واسطے دیتے تھے کہ ان کے شر و فساد سے مسلمان بچے رہیں ۔ (۳) وہ لوگ جو اسلام لائے مگر ان کا اعتقاد کمر ور تھا تو ان کو اس واسطے عطا کرتے کہ ثابت قدم رہیں۔ مؤلفۃ القلوب میں نمایاں لوگ یہ ہیں عیینہ بن حصن اقرع بن حابس، عباس بن مرد اس یہ تینوں سرداران قریش میں سے ہیں ان کے علاوہ ابو سفیان محتر بن حرب اموی حارث بن ہشام مخزومی عبدالرحمن بن مر بوع مخزومی سہیل بن عمر والعامری حويطب بن عبد العزی عامری عبد العزیٰ اسدی، حکیم بن حزام اسدی وغیرہ ہیں۔ مؤلفۃ القلوب عہد رسالت میں تھے مگر صدیق اکبر کے عہد خلافت میں منقطع ہو گئے۔ (اخرجہ ابن ابی شیبة عن العمی ) چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ عیینہ بن حصن فزاری اور اقرع بن حابس تمیمی دونوں حضرت ابو بکر کے پاس اپنی زمین کے واسطے معافی لینے آئے پس صدیق اکبر نے فرمان لکھ دیا پھر دونوں حضرت عمر کے پاس گواہی کو لائے تو آپ نے وہ فرمان چاک کر دیا اور کہا کہ یہ تو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم تم کو اس لئے دیتے تھے تا کہ وہ اسلام کی طرف تمہارے دلوں کی تالیف فرمادیں اور اب اللہ تعالیٰ نے اسلام کو غالب اور تم سے بے پرواہ کر دیا ہے پس اگر تم اسلام پر ثابت قدم رہو تو بہتر ہے ورنہ ہمارے تمہارے درمیان تلوار فیصلہ ہے وہ دونوں لوٹ کر حضرت ابوبکر کے پاس گئے اور کہا کہ آپ خلیفہ ہیں یا عمر آپ نے فرمایا انشاء اللہ وہ خلیفہ ہے۔ صدیق اکبر نے ، حضرت عمر کے اس فیصلے کے ساتھ موافقت کی ، اس وقت سے مؤلفہ القلوب کا حق منقطع ہو گیا اور چونکہ صحابہ میں سے کسی نے اس پر انکار نہیں کیا بلکہ سب نے سکوت اختیار فرمایا تو گویا مؤلفۃ القلوب کے سقوط پر صحابہ کا اجماع سکوتی بھی منعقد ہو گیا ہے۔ (فتح القدیر)
The book of Zakat. Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume Three. (4) Mu'allafatu al-Qulub: those from whom Islam is hoped or who are weak in Islam. (5) Riqab: meaning slaves whose kitabah (contract of manumission) is paid to free them, or they are bought and freed, or captives are ransomed and released. (6) Gharimin: those who are burdened with debt due to some calamity or became indebted, or who are burdened regarding some surety etc. (7) Fi Sabilillah: assistance for those going for jihad etc. (8) Ibn al-Sabil: a traveler who, while traveling, does not possess the nisab, even if he has wealth at home. (Murshid Thanwi) The author of Hidayah says: From these eight categories, one category, Mu'allafatu al-Qulub, has fallen (is abrogated), meaning after the demise of the Prophet (peace be upon him), this category no longer exists. In al-Inayah: There were three types of Mu'allafatu al-Qulub: (1) Those disbelievers to whom the Prophet would give so that their hearts would incline towards Islam through this worldly pittance. (2) Those disbelievers to whom he would give so that Muslims would be safe from their evil and mischief. (3) Those who had embraced Islam but their belief was weak, so they were given so that they would remain steadfast. Prominent individuals among Mu'allafatu al-Qulub include: 'Uyaynah ibn Hisn, al-Aqra' ibn Habis, 'Abbas ibn Mardas – these three were from the chiefs of Quraysh. Besides them, Abu Sufyan ibn Harb al-Umawi, al-Harith ibn Hisham al-Makhzumi, 'Abdul-Rahman ibn Murra al-Makhzumi, Suhayl ibn 'Amr al-'Amiri, Huyayyib ibn 'Abdul-'Azzi al-'Amiri, 'Abdul-'Uzza al-Asadi, Hakim ibn Hizam al-Asadi, and others. Mu'allafatu al-Qulub existed during the time of the Messengership, but they were discontinued during the caliphate of al-Siddiq al-Akbar. (Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah from al-['Ummi?]) Thus it is narrated that 'Uyaynah ibn Hisn al-Fazari and al-Aqra' ibn Habis al-Tamimi came to Abu Bakr to get remission for their land. So al-Siddiq wrote a decree. Then both brought it to 'Umar (as witness) who tore up the decree and said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to give this to you so that he might reconcile your hearts to Islam, and now Allah has made Islam dominant and independent of you. So if you remain steadfast on Islam, it is better; otherwise, between you and us is the sword as judge. They returned to Abu Bakr and said: Are you the caliph or 'Umar? He replied: Insha'Allah, he is the caliph. Al-Siddiq agreed with this decision of 'Umar. From that time, the right of Mu'allafatu al-Qulub was cut off, and since none of the Companions objected to it, but rather all remained silent, thus a tacit consensus (ijma sukuti) of the Companions was established on the abrogation of Mu'allafatu al-Qulub. (Fath al-Qadir)
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains a key historical development in the fiqh of zakat. The author first lists the eight categories of zakat recipients as derived from Quran 9:60. He then focuses on the category of Mu'allafatu al-Qulub, stating that it was a specific dispensation during the Prophet's lifetime, designed to win hearts to Islam or to protect Muslims from harm. After the Prophet's death and with the strengthening of Islam, the Caliph 'Umar, with the concurrence of Abu Bakr, discontinued this category, and the Companions' silence constituted a tacit ijma. This ruling is now settled: Mu'allafatu al-Qulub is not a valid category for zakat distribution in our time. The passage also provides historical names and demonstrates how fiqh rulings can change with the change of circumstances (taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman).

Key Terms
مؤلفة القلوب (Mu'allafatu al-Qulub): A category of zakat recipients whose hearts are to be reconciled to Islam. This includes three types: disbelievers hoped for conversion, disbelievers feared for their harm, and weak Muslims needing encouragement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the category of Mu'allafatu al-Qulub no longer valid for zakat distribution according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Prophet prohibited it in his final sermon.
B) Because the Companions, particularly Umar and Abu Bakr, discontinued it and others remained silent, forming an ijma.
C) Because there are no longer any poor Muslims who need zakat.
D) Because the Quranic verse was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Mu'allafatu al-Qulub is abrogated as a zakat category by the tacit consensus (ijma sukuti) of the Companions, a ruling still followed in the Hanafi school.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
6 min
Hanafi and Shafi'i Dispute on the Definition of Faqir and Miskin
Defining Faqir and Miskin with proofs, presenting Hanafi and Shafi'i positions with responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i definitions of Faqir and Miskin, cite the Quranic proofs for each, explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument, and apply the ruling to determine priority in zakat distribution.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, Miskin is poorer than Faqir; the opposite in Shafi'i, changing zakat priority.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute over the definitions of Faqir and Miskin, two categories of zakat recipients. The Hanafi school, following Imam Abu Hanifa, defines Miskin as the more destitute, while Imam al-Shafi'i reverses the order. Through Quranic proofs and responses, we will uncover the reasoning behind each position and its practical impact on zakat distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute is about which of Faqir and Miskin is more destitute, affecting zakat priority.
This is a definitional dispute with practical consequences.
2
State the Hanafi definition and proof
Hanafi: Miskin has nothing, Faqir has less than nisab. Proof from Quran 90:16 and 2:273.
Quran 90:16 describes Miskin as 'full of dust'; Quran 2:273 describes Fuqara as appearing wealthy due to self-restraint.
3
State the Shafi'i definition and proof
Shafi'i: Faqir has nothing, Miskin has some property. Proof from Quran 18:79 referring to ship owners as Miskin.
The ship 'belonged to Miskin' suggests ownership.
4
Analyze the Hanafi responses to the Shafi'i proof
Three responses: (1) Using 'Miskin' out of mercy/compassion, (2) The workers were employees, not owners, (3) The ship was on loan ('ariyah).
The Prophet's dua to be a Miskin while seeking refuge from poverty supports the mercy interpretation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In Hanafi, priority in zakat goes to Miskin; in Shafi'i, to Faqir.
Abu Yusuf holds they are one category, but the mufta bihi is two independent categories.

فقیر اور مسکین کی تعریف
والْفَقِيرُ مَن لَهُ أدْنى شيءٌ وَالْمِسْكِينُ مَنْ لا شَيْء لَهُ وَهَذَا مَرُويٌّ عَنْ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَدْ قِيلَ على العكس ولكل وَجْهٌ ثُمَّ هُمَا صِنفان أو صِنف وَاحِدٌ سَنَذَكُرُهُ فِى كِتَابِ الْوَصَايَا إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى
ترجمہ اور فقیر وہ شخص ہے جس کے پاس کمتر چیز ہو اور مسکین وہ ہے جس کے پاس کچھ نہ ہو۔ اور یہ قول ابوحنیفہ سے مروی ہے۔ اور اس کے برعکس بھی کہا گیا ہے اور ہر قول کے واسطے دلیل موجود ہے پھر فقیر اور مسکین دو صنف ہیں یا ایک ہی قسم ہے ہم اس کو انشاء اللہ کتاب الوصایا میں ذکر کریں گے۔ تشریح فقیر اور مسکین کی تعریف میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہے چنانچہ حضرت امام اعظم سے مروی ہے کہ فقیر وہ شخص ہے جس کے پاس کچھ ہومگر نصاب سے کم ہو۔ یا بقدر نصاب ہومگر وہ نصاب غیر نامی ہو۔ اور یہ خود اپنی ضروریات میں گھرا ہوا ہے اور مسکین وہ ہے جس کے پاس قطعا کوئی چیز نہ ہو نہ اس کے پاس نان شبینہ ہے اور نہ تن ڈھکنے کے لئے کپڑا ہے گویا امام صاحب کے نزدیک مسکین زیادہ خستہ حال ہوتا ہے بہ نسبت فقیر کے۔
امام شافعی کا مذہب اس کے برعکس ہے یعنی ان کے نزدیک مسکین کے مقابلہ میں فقیر کی حالت زیادہ خراب اور خستہ ہوتی ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول " أَمَّا السَّفِينَةُ فَكَانَتْ لِمَسَاكِينَ (الكهف ۷۹) ہے یعنی حضرت خضر علیہ السلام نے جس کشتی کو عیب دار کیا تھا وہ مسکینوں کے تھی، دیکھئے اس آیت میں کشتی کے مالکوں کو مسکین کہا گیا ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسکین کے پاس کچھ نہ کچھ ہوتا ہے اور فقیر کے پاس کچھ نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا مسکین کی بہ نسبت فقیر زیادہ خستہ حال ہوا۔
حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے أَوْ مِسْكِينًا ذَا مَتْرَبَةٍ ( البلد ١٦) یعنی مسکین جو خاک آلود ہے مطلب یہ ہے کہ مسکین بھوک سے اور برہنہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اپنا پیٹ زمین پر لگائے رکھتا ہے اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسکین کے پاس نہ سد رمق کھانا ہوتا ہے اور نہ تن چھپانے کے لئے کپڑا ہوتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ مسکین کی حالت فقیر کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ خستہ ہوتی ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الَّذِينَ أُحْصِرُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ لَا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ ضَرْبًا فِي الْأَرْضِ يَحْسَبُهُمُ الْجَاهِلُ أَغْنِيَاءَ مِنَ التَّعَفُّفِ تَعْرِفُهُم بِسِيمَاهُمْ لَا يَسْأَلُونَ النَّاسَ إِلْحَافًا (البقرة ٢٧٣) خیرات ان لوگوں کے لئے ہے جو رکے ہوئے ہیں اللہ کی راہ میں چل پھر نہیں سکتے ملک میں سمجھے انکو نا واقف مالدار ان کے سوال نہ کرنے سے تو پہچانتا ہے ان کو ان کے چہرے سے نہیں سوال کرتے لوگوں سے لپٹ کر ۔ اس آیت میں ان کو ایسا فقیر کہا ہے کہ سوال نہ کرنے سے ناواقف آدمی ان کو مالدار خیال کرتا ہے۔ اور یہ بات اس وقت ممکن ہوگی جبکہ اس کا ظاہر حال اچھا ہو۔ اور جب ظاہر حال اچھا ہوا تو معلوم ہوا کہ فقیر کے پاس کچھ نہ کچھ ضرور ہوتا ہے اس سے بھی حضرت امام صاحب کے قول کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔
امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ آیت أَمَّا السَّفِينَةُ فَكَانَتْ لِمَسَاكِينَ (الكهف ۷۹) کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے کشتی کے مالکوں کو ترحم اور شفقت کے پیش نظر مسکین کہا ہے جیسے ایک بار رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا " اللَّهُمَّ أَحْيِنِي مِسْكِينًا وَأَمِتْنِي مِسْكِينًا وَاحْشُرْنِي فِي زُمْرَةِ الْمَسَاكِينِ " اے اللہ مجھ کو مسکین بنا کر زندہ رکھ اور موت دے تو مسکین ہونے کی حالت میں اور میرا حشر بھی زمرہ مساکین میں فرمایا حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مسکین ہونے کی دعا فرمائی ہے حالانکہ آپ نے فقر اور تنگدستی سے پناہ مانگی ہے یہ دونوں باتیں اس طرح جمع ہو سکتی ہیں کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جس فقر سے پناہ مانگی ہے وہ نفس اور دل کا فقر ہے اور مسکین ہونے کی دعا ترحم کے لئے ہے یعنی خدایا مجھے کو ایسا مسکین بنا جو رحم اور شفقت کا مستحق ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ کشتی مساکین کی ملک نہیں تھی بلکہ یہ لوگ اس کشتی میں مزدوری کیا کرتے تھے اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ خضر علیہ السلام کے پیش نظر کشتی کو عیب دار کرنے سے یہ تھا کہ ان مساکین کا روز گار ختم نہ ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ اگر کشتی صحیح سالم چھوڑ دی جاتی اور بادشاہ اپنی عادت کے مطابق اس کو غصب کر لیتا تو بچارے یہ مساکین بے روزگار ہو کر رہ جاتے تیسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ کشتی ان کے پاس عاریہ تھی نہ کہ یہ لوگ اس کے مالک تھے بہر حال یہ آیت اس پر دلالت نہیں کرتی کہ مسکین کے پاس کچھ نہ کچھ ہوتا ہے رہی یہ بات کہ فقیر اور مسکین دونوں ایک قسم ہیں یا دو قسم ہیں تو اس کی تفصیل تو کتاب الوصایا میں آئیگی لیکن یہاں اتنا عرض ہے کہ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک فقیر اور مسکین مستقل دو قسمیں ہیں اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک دونوں مل کر ایک قسم ہے
The definition of Faqir and Miskin. 'The Faqir is the one who possesses the minimum thing, and the Miskin is the one who possesses nothing. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa. And the opposite has also been said, and each has a basis. Then, are they two categories or one category? We will mention it in the Book of Wasiyyah, if Allah wills. Translation: Faqir is the person who has a little something, and Miskin is the one who has nothing. This saying is narrated from Abu Hanifa. And the opposite has also been said, and each saying has proof. Then, Faqir and Miskin are two categories or one category? We will mention it in the Book of Wasiyyah, inshaAllah. Explanation: There is a difference of opinion among the Imams regarding the definition of Faqir and Miskin. It is narrated from Imam A'zam that Faqir is a person who has something, but it is less than the nisab, or it equals the nisab but that nisab is non-productive (ghayr nami). And he is himself wrapped up in his necessities. And Miskin is the one who has absolutely nothing, neither food for the night nor clothing to cover himself. So according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the Miskin is more destitute than the Faqir. The school of Imam Shafi'i is the reverse: according to him, the Faqir is in a worse and more destitute state than the Miskin. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the saying of Allah, the Exalted, 'As for the ship, it belonged to the Miskin' (Surah al-Kahf 79). That is, the ship which Khidr (alayhissalam) damaged belonged to Miskin. Note that in this verse, the owners of the ship are called Miskin. From this it is understood that a Miskin possesses something, while the Faqir possesses nothing. Therefore, the Faqir is more destitute than the Miskin. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that Allah, the Exalted, said, 'Or a Miskin full of dust' (Surah al-Balad 16). That is, a Miskin who is covered with dust. The meaning is that a Miskin, due to hunger and nakedness, keeps his stomach on the ground. From this verse it is understood that a Miskin has neither food to sustain life nor clothing to cover himself. So it is established that the condition of a Miskin is more destitute than that of a Faqir. The second proof is that Allah, the Exalted, said, '(Charity is) for the poor (Fuqara) who are confined in the way of Allah, unable to travel through the land; the ignorant considers them wealthy because of their self-restraint; you will recognize them by their mark; they do not ask people persistently' (Surah al-Baqarah 273). In this verse, they are called such Fuqara that the ignorant person considers them wealthy due to their not asking. And this is only possible when their external condition is good. And when the external condition is good, it becomes clear that a Faqir certainly possesses something. This also supports the speech of Imam Abu Hanifa. The response to the verse presented by Imam Shafi'i, 'As for the ship, it belonged to Miskin' (Surah al-Kahf 79) is that Allah called the owners of the ship Miskin out of mercy and compassion, just as once the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'O Allah, keep me alive as a Miskin, cause me to die as a Miskin, and resurrect me among the group of Miskin.' This hadith shows that the Prophet prayed to be a Miskin, whereas he sought refuge from poverty and destitution. These two things can be reconciled as follows: the poverty from which the Prophet sought refuge is the poverty of the self and heart, and the prayer to be a Miskin is for mercy, i.e., O Allah, make me such a Miskin who deserves mercy and compassion. The second response is that the ship was not owned by the Miskin; rather, these people worked for wages on the ship. So the meaning is that Khidr's intention in damaging the ship was that the livelihood of these Miskin should not come to an end, because if the ship were left intact and the king seized it by force, as was his habit, these poor Miskin would become unemployed. The third response is that the ship was given to them as a loan ('ariyah), not that they owned it. In any case, this verse does not indicate that a Miskin possesses something. As for the question whether Faqir and Miskin are one category or two categories, the detail will come in the Book of Wasiyyah, but here (we say) that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Faqir and Miskin are two independent categories, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf, both together constitute one category.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah delves into the definitions of two key terms in the Quranic verse on zakat expenditure: Faqir and Miskin. The Hanafi school, based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view, defines Faqir as someone who possesses some property but it is below the zakat threshold (nisab) or is non-productive. Miskin is someone with absolutely no property, making him the poorer of the two. Imam Shafi'i holds the opposite view: Miskin is one who has some property, while Faqir has none. The text presents the proofs from the Quran for both positions. For Hanafi: Surah al-Balad (90:16) describes a Miskin as 'full of dust,' indicating extreme poverty. Surah al-Baqarah (2:273) describes Fuqara who appear wealthy due to self-restraint, implying they have some property. For Shafi'i: Surah al-Kahf (18:79) refers to shipowners as Miskin, implying they own a ship. The passage then provides Hanafi responses to the Shafi'i argument, including a structural analysis (the term was used out of mercy), a contextual analysis (the workers were mere employees not owners), and a juristic analysis (the ship was on loan). This dispute has practical implications: the order of priority in distributing zakat will differ. The textbook ends by noting that Abu Yusuf considers them one category, but the Hanafi position is that they are two distinct categories. This passage is an excellent example of inter-madhhab debate with textual evidence.

Key Terms
فقير (faqir): According to Imam Abu Hanifa, a person who possesses something but it is less than the zakat nisab or equals nisab but is non-productive (ghayr nami).
مسكين (miskin): According to Imam Abu Hanifa, a person who has absolutely nothing, not even food or clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is more deserving of zakat: a Faqir or a Miskin?
A) Faqir
B) Miskin
C) Both equally
D) It depends on the amount of zakat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Miskin is needier than Faqir, based on Quranic evidence, and this affects zakat priority.

The Zakat Collector's Payment: Kifayah, Not Fixed Share
Ruling on zakat collector's payment and Hashimi exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the zakat collector's payment, explain the basis of kifayah, and distinguish the Hashimi exception.

Core Idea
The zakat collector's payment is a maintenance allowance, not a wage — based on need, not a fixed fraction.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on compensating the zakat collector. While the collector is entitled to payment even if wealthy, the amount is determined by sufficiency (kifayah), not a predetermined share like one-eighth. This distinguishes the Hanafi school from the Shafi'i school. Additionally, a critical exception is made for Hashimi collectors to preserve the dignity of the Prophet's lineage.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its hukm level
Identify that the imam must pay the collector and his helpers. The hukm is wajib upon the imam from the zakat funds.
The obligation arises because the collector has confined himself for public service.
2
Identify the basis of payment
The payment is based on kifayah (sufficiency), not a fixed wage. Understand why: the collector is analogous to judges and fighters whose maintenance is obligatory on the community.
This is proven by qiyas: asl = judge/fighter, far' = collector, illa = public service.
3
Recognize the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds a fixed one-eighth share. The Hanafi response is that the Quranic verse (9:60) does not specify a fixed share; the collector's entitlement is for work done, not a percentage.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Shafi'i, always one-eighth; under Hanafi, variable based on need.
4
Apply the Hashimi exception
A Hashimi collector cannot take payment due to the suspicion (shubha) of sadaqah, which is impure for the Prophet's family. A rich non-Hashimi may take despite wealth because he does not share that honor.
The exception shows consideration for the honor of the Prophet's lineage.
5
Note practical implications
The imam determines the amount based on needs. If no work is done (e.g., people bring zakat directly), the collector gets nothing. The payment is not ijarah but a maintenance allowance.
If the needs consume all collected zakat, half is the maximum paid to the collector.

بھی ذہن نشین رہے کہ عامل کو جو کچھ دیا جاتا ہے وہ اجارہ کے طور پر نہیں دیا جاتا کیونکہ اجارہ کے لئے عمل کو معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے مدت اور اجرت کا معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے اور یہاں کچھ بھی معلوم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے عامل کو اجرت کے طور پر نہیں دیا جائے گا بلکہ جتنا وقت اس کا آنے جانے اور صدقات وصول کرنے میں صرف ہوا ہے اس وقت کا مکمل خرچ دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اس نے اپنے آپ کو اس کام کے لئے محبوس کر دیا ہے اور جو شخص اپنے آپ کو امور مسلمین کے کاموں کے لئے فارغ کر دے تو اس کا نان نفقہ انہیں پر واجب ہوتا ہے جیسے قاضیوں اور قتال کرنے والوں کا نفقہ عامتہ المسلمین پر واجب ہوتا ہے اور بیوی کا نفقہ شوہر پر واجب ہوتا ہے جب یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ عامل کو بطور اجرت نہیں دیا جاتا تو بقدر کفایت جو کچھ اس کو دیا جائے گا وہ آٹھویں حصہ وغیرہ کسی مخصوص مقدار کے ساتھ بھی متعین نہیں ہوگا یعنی یہ نہ ہوگا کہ عامل نے جو زکوۃ وصول کی ہے اس کا آٹھواں حصہ اس کو دیدیا جائے گا جیسا کہ امام شافعی نے
The imam pays the collector if he worked, according to his work, giving him what suffices him and his helpers, not determined by one-eighth, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because his entitlement is by way of sufficiency. Therefore, he takes even if he is rich, except that there is a suspicion of sadaqah, so the Hashimi collector does not take it, to keep the kinship of the Messenger (peace be upon him) free from the suspicion of filth. And the rich person does not equal him in entitlement to honor, so the suspicion is not considered in his case. Translation: The imam gives the collector if he worked according to his work; so the imam gives him an amount that suffices him and his helpers, not fixed at one-eighth, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the collector's entitlement is by way of sufficiency. For this reason, he takes it even if he is rich. However, since there is a suspicion of sadaqah, the Hashimi collector does not take it, to keep the kinship of the Messenger (peace be upon him) free from the suspicion of filth. And the rich person does not equal him in entitlement to honor, so the suspicion is not considered in his case. Explanation: In the Quran, the third category of zakat expenditure is 'amilin' (collectors). 'Amilin' is the plural of 'amil': the person appointed by the imam of the Muslims to collect sadaqat etc. The collector is also called 'sa'i'. The imam gives the collector and his helpers according to their work, but he ensures he gives what suffices them. If the needs of the collector and his helpers encompass the entire zakat collected, then he is not given more than half. If people bring their zakat voluntarily to the imam, then the collector is not entitled to anything, because the collector is given due to his work, and if no work occurred, he is not entitled. Also note: what the collector is given is not as an ijarah (hire), because ijarah requires the work to be known, the period and wage known, and here nothing is known. Therefore, he is not given as a wage, but rather the complete expenditure for the time he spent coming and going and collecting the sadaqat is given, because he has confined himself for this work. And whoever frees himself for the works of the Muslims, his maintenance is obligatory upon them, just as the maintenance of judges and fighters is obligatory upon the general Muslims, and the wife's maintenance is obligatory upon the husband. When it is established that the collector is not given as a wage, then what he is given according to sufficiency is not determined by one-eighth or any other fixed amount; meaning it is not that one-eighth of the zakat he collects is given to him, as Imam al-Shafi'i says...
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the zakat collector (amil) and his payment. It comes from the commentary on the Hidayah. The matn states that the imam pays the collector according to his work, giving him and his helpers what suffices them, and that this amount is not fixed at one-eighth of the collected zakat. This is contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i, who specifies one-eighth. The Hanafi position is based on the principle that the collector's entitlement is by way of sufficiency (kifayah), not fixed remuneration. Therefore, even a rich collector can take if he worked, because it is a right for his service. However, there is an exception: a Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) collector cannot take this payment, to keep the Prophet's lineage free from the suspicion of sadaqah (which is impure due to being the dirt of people's wealth). But a rich non-Hashimi collector can take because he does not share the special honor of the Hashimi lineage; the suspicion is not considered in his case. The commentary elaborates: The imam gives the collector and his helpers enough to cover their needs, but if their needs consume the entire zakat, they get no more than half. If people bring zakat directly to the imam without the collector's work, the collector gets nothing. The payment is not an ijarah (hire) because the work and duration are unspecified; rather, it is a maintenance allowance (nafaqah) akin to that of judges and fighters, whose maintenance is obligatory on the general Muslim populace. Thus, the collector's payment is not fixed as one-eighth, contrary to Shafi'i's school.

Key Terms
عامل (ʿāmil): A person appointed by the imam to collect zakat and other sadaqat from the people.
هاشمي (hāshimī): A descendant of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ from the Banu Hashim clan.
كفاية (kifāyah): Sufficiency: an amount that meets the basic needs of the collector and his helpers for the duration they are engaged in the work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The zakat collector's payment is a maintenance allowance (kifayah), not a fixed wage; and the Hashimi collector is excluded to preserve the honor of the Prophet's lineage.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Fuqara and Masakin Categories
Intra-Hanafi dispute example on will distribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the classification of fuqara and masakin, and apply the rule to a will distribution scenario.

Core Idea
Fuqara and masakin are separate categories according to Abu Hanifa, but one category according to Abu Yusuf.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf over whether the poor (fuqara) and the needy (masakin) are distinct categories or a single group. The dispute is illustrated with a concrete example: a person bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zaid, the poor, and the needy. The classification determines how many shares the third is divided into. Understanding this difference is essential for applying Hanafi inheritance and zakat rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a will where one-third of the testator's wealth is left for Zaid, the poor (fuqara), and the needy (masakin).
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, fuqara and masakin together form one category. Thus, the third is divided into two halves: half for Zaid and half for the combined group of poor and needy.
Abu Yusuf treats them as a single category.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, fuqara and masakin are two separate categories. Thus, the third is divided into three equal shares: one for Zaid, one for the poor, and one for the needy.
Abu Hanifa distinguishes them.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the number of shares: Abu Yusuf gives two shares (Zaid, and the combined group), while Abu Hanifa gives three (Zaid, fuqara, masakin). This affects how much each recipient receives.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is the distribution pattern.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شمر اختلاف اس مثال میں ظاہر ہوگا۔ کہ ایک شخص نے اپنے نکث مال کی وصیت زید اور فقراء اور مساکین کے لئے کی تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ثلث مال کا آدھا زید کو دیا جائے گا اور آدھا فقراء اور مساکین کو دیدیا جائے گا کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک فقراء اور مساکین دونوں مل کر ایک قسم ہیں۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس ثلث مال کو تین حصوں میں تقسیم کر کے ایک حصہ زید کو دیں گے اور ایک فقراء کو اور ایک مساکین کو دیں گے کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک فقراء اور مساکین دو الگ الگ قسم ہیں۔
The difference will appear in this example: a person made a will of one-third of his wealth for Zaid and the poor and the needy. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, half of the third will be given to Zaid and half to the poor and needy, because in his view the poor and the needy together are one category. According to Imam Sahib, the third is divided into three parts: one part to Zaid, one to the poor, and one to the needy, because in his view the poor and the needy are two separate categories.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the classification of fuqara (poor) and masakin (needy) in the context of a will. The example shows that if someone bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zaid and to the poor and needy, the distribution differs based on whether they are considered one group or two. Abu Yusuf treats them as a single category, so half goes to Zaid and half to the combined group. Abu Hanifa treats them as distinct, so the third is split into three equal shares. This difference has practical implications for distributing zakat and wills in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
فقراء (fuqara): The poor – those who have less than the needy or are in extreme poverty.
مساکین (masakin): The needy – those who have some means but are still insufficient.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest or will regarding disposal of up to one-third of property after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, fuqara and masakin are distinct categories per the relied-upon view, affecting how bequests and zakat are distributed.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Ruling on Payment to Zakat Collector (Amil)
Explanation of the amil's compensation and rebuttal of Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the amil's compensation and explain the evidence that it is based on sufficiency (kifayah) rather than a fixed share.

Core Idea
The amil is paid by sufficiency, not a fixed eighth, because his entitlement is for work, not as a zakat recipient.

This passage deals with the payment of the zakat collector (amil). It clarifies that the Imam gives him an amount sufficient for him and his helpers, not a fixed share of the collected zakat. The Hanafi school argues that this payment is compensation for work, not a zakat disbursement, and supports this with key evidence: a wealthy amil still receives payment, and if the owner delivers zakat directly to the Imam, the amil gets nothing. The passage also explains why a Hashimi amil is excluded due to the suspicion of charity (shubhat al-sadaqah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its nature
Recognize that the passage states a ruling regarding the amil's payment: the Imam must pay the amil from zakat funds based on the work performed, sufficient for him and his helpers. This is a wajib obligation on the Imam.
The payment is not a fixed share; it varies according to need.
2
Understand the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the amil's entitlement is by way of kifayah (sufficiency), not as a recipient of zakat. Therefore, the amount is not fixed at one-eighth, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i.
3
Examine the proofs (dalil)
Two proofs are presented: 1) The amil takes even if he is rich, which would not be allowed if he were a zakat recipient. 2) If the owner delivers zakat directly to the Imam without the amil's work, the amil receives nothing, showing it is compensation for work.
These proofs demonstrate that the payment is remuneration, not a charitable share.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i opposition
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the amil is entitled to a fixed one-eighth (or one-seventh after dropping mu'allafah) of the collected zakat, based on the eight categories in the Quran (Surah al-Tawbah, 9:60).
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The Hanafi position is preferred because it aligns with the nature of the amil's work and avoids the inconsistency of a wealthy amil receiving a zakat share. The text explicitly refutes the Shafi'i view.

Source Text

عامل کو بقدر عمل دیا جائے گا، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر ، ہاشمی عامل مصرف زکوۃ نہیں
وَالْعَامِلُ يَدْفَعُ الْإِمَامُ إِلَيْهِ إِنْ عَمِلَ بِقَدْرِ عَمَلِهِ فَيُعْطِيهِ مَا يَسَعُهُ وَأَعْوَ انهُ غَيْرَ مُقَدِّرِ بِالثَّمَنِ خِلَافَا لِلشَّافِعِي لأَنَّ اِسْتِحْقَاقَهُ بِطَرِيْقِ الْكِفَايَةِ وَلِهَذَا يَأْخُذُ وَإِنْ كَانَ غَنِيَّا إِلَّا أَنَّ فِيهِ شُهَةَ الصَّدَقَةِ فَلَا يَأْخُدُهَا الْعَامِلُ الهَاشِمِيُّ تَنْزِيْهَا لِقَرَابَةِ الرَّسُولِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَنْ شُبْهَةِ الْوَسَخِ وَالْغَنِيُّ لَا يُوَازِيهِ فِى اِسْتِحْقَاقِ الْكَرَامَةِ فَلَمْ تُعتبر الشُّبهة في حقه

إِلَّا انَّ فِيْه شُهَةَ الصَّدَقَةِ .. الخ سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے اعتراض یہ ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ عامل کا استحقاق بطریق کفایت ہے نہ کہ بطریق زکوۃ تو عامل اگر ہاشمی گھرانے کا ہو تو اس کے لئے بھی بقدر عمل زکوۃ کے مال سے لینا جائز ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ ہاشمی کے لئے بالکل جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ چونکہ زکوۃ ادا کرنے کرنے والے کے ذمہ سے زکوۃ ساقط ہوئی ہے اس لئے اس مال میں بھی صدقہ کا شبہ پایا گیا اور جب صدقہ کا شبہ پایا گیا تو خاندان رسالت کو ز کوۃ اور صدقہ کے میل و یچیل سے پاک وصاف رکھنے کے لئے ہاشمی عامل کو اس میں سے کچھ نہ دیا جائے گا لیکن اس پر پھر اعتراض ہو گا کہ جس طرح ہاشمی کے لئے زکوۃ کا مال لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے مالدار کے لئے بھی جائز نہیں ہے پس جس طرح ہاشمی عامل نہیں لے گا اسی طرح مالدار عامل کو بھی نہ لینا چاہئے تھا جواب بغیر ہاشمی مالدار مستحق کرامت ہونے میں ہاشمی کے برابر نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے صدقہ کے شبہ کا ہاشمی کے حق میں اعتبار کیا گیا ہے اور غیر ہاشمی مالدار کے حق میں اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔
The amil will be given according to his work. The Imam will give him if he has worked according to his work; he will give him what suffices him and his helpers, not fixed as one-eighth, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because his entitlement is by way of sufficiency. Therefore he takes even if he is rich, except that there is a suspicion of charity, so the Hashimi amil will not take it, to purify the kinship of the Messenger (upon him peace) from the suspicion of filth. The rich person is not equivalent to him in entitlement to honor, so the suspicion is not considered in his case. [...]
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the zakat collector (amil). It begins by stating that the amil is paid by the Imam based on the work performed, sufficient for him and his helpers, and this amount is not fixed as one-eighth — contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i who considers it a fixed share. The Hanafi position is that the amil's entitlement is by way of kifayah (sufficiency), not as a share of zakat. Evidence: if the owner delivers zakat directly to the Imam, the amil gets nothing; also, a rich amil still takes, which would not be the case if it were a zakat share. However, a Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) amil cannot take because of the suspicion of charity, as they are prohibited from taking sadaqah. A non-Hashimi rich amil can take because he is not equal to a Hashimi in honor. The payment is not wages (ijarah) because the work and payment are unspecified; rather, it is maintenance (nafaqah) for those who dedicate themselves to Muslim affairs.

Key Terms
عامل (amil): The person appointed by the Imam to collect zakat and other charitable funds.
کفایت (kifayah): Sufficiency – the amount needed to cover the amil's expenses and those of his helpers.
شبهة الصدقة (shubhat al-sadaqah): The suspicion or semblance of charity in the zakat funds, which prohibits Hashimi from taking it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a Hashimi amil not take payment from zakat funds according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because Hashimi are not allowed to work as amils.
B) Because there is a suspicion of charity (shubhat al-sadaqah) in the funds.
C) Because they are not entitled to any payment.
D) Because they must receive a fixed share instead.

Key Takeaway
The amil's compensation is based on sufficiency, not a fixed share, because it is remuneration for work, not a zakat disbursement, and a Hashimi amil is exempted due to the suspicion of charity.

Zakat for Riqab: Assisting Mukatib
Clarification that fi al-riqab means assisting mukatib, not purchasing slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi interpretation of fi al-riqab in zakat and distinguish it from the alternative view of purchasing slaves.

Core Idea
Zakat for riqab is given to mukatib, not to buy slaves—ownership transfer to a recipient is essential.

The fourth category of zakat expenditure is 'fi al-riqab'. In this lesson, we examine two possible interpretations: purchasing slaves to free them, or assisting mukatib (slaves under a manumission contract) to pay their freedom price. The Hanafi school, following transmitted authority, adopts the second view and explains why the first fails to meet zakat's essential condition of transferring ownership to the recipient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Zakat Category
Locate the phrase 'fi al-riqab' in the passage. The text explains it as the fourth category of zakat expenditure.
The verse of zakat (9:60) lists eight categories; this is one of them.
2
Recognize the Two Interpretations
The passage mentions two possible meanings: (1) purchasing slaves and freeing them, (2) helping a mukatib pay off his contract.
These represent a legitimate ikhtilaf (disagreement) in interpretation.
3
Understand the Hanafi Choice
The text, following al-Quduri and transmissions from early scholars, chooses the second interpretation: assisting mukatib.
This is called the transmitted (manqul) interpretation and is the mufta bihi position.
4
Grasp the Legal Reason
The reason given is that for zakat to be valid, ownership of the zakat payment must be transferred to the recipient. A slave (who is not a mukatib) cannot own property, so paying to purchase and free a slave does not transfer ownership to the slave; instead, the money goes to the seller. Only a mukatib has the legal capacity to own and can receive zakat directly to pay his master.
This is a key Hanafi usul point: the condition of tamlik (granting ownership) applies to zakat.
5
Distinguish from the Alternative
Contrast the Hanafi view with the alternative: purchasing slaves to free them would not fulfill the zakat obligation because the recipient (the slave) does not become owner of the zakat amount.
Other schools may differ, but the Hanafi school consistently applies the tamlik condition here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِى الرِّقَابِ أَنْ يُعَانَ الْمُكَاتِبُونَ مِنْهَا فِى فَتِ رِقَابِهِمْ هُوَ الْمَنْقُولُ
ترجمہ اور گردنوں کے چھڑانے میں وہ یہ ہے کہ مکاتبوں کی ان کی گردنوں کے چھڑانے میں اعانت کی جائے یہی تفسیر منقول ہے۔ شریح مصارف زکوۃ کی چوتھی قسم وفی الرقاب ہے اس کی تفسیر میں دو صورتیں بیان کی گئیں میں ایک یہ کہ زکوۃ کے مال سے غلام خرید کر آزاد کیا جائے۔ دوم یہ کہ مکاتب کی بدل کتابت ادا کرنے میں مدد کی جائے۔ صاحب قدوری نے اسی دوسری صورت کو اختیار کیا ہے اور طبرانی میں حسن بصری ، امام زہری اور عبدالرحمن بن یزید بن اسلم سے بھی وفی الرقاب کی یہی تفسیر ہے چنانچہ ان حضرات نے فرمایا ہے وَفِي الرِّقَابِ هُمُ الْمُكَاتُبُونَ يعنى وَفِي الرِّقَابِ سے مراد یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ کی رقم مکاتب کو دیدی جائے تا کہ وہ اپنے مولیٰ کو بدل کتابت ادا کر کے اپنی گردن چھڑا لے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر زکوۃ کی رقم سے غلام خرید کر آزاد کیا جائے تو زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی کیونکہ ادائے زکوۃ کے لئے ما لک کر دینا شرط ہے اور اس صورت میں مالک کو دینے کے معنی نہیں پائے گئے کیونکہ خالص غلام کے اندر مالک بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔
And in [the category of] necks: that the mukatibun be helped from it in freeing their necks; this is the transmitted [interpretation]. Translation: And regarding the freeing of necks, it is that the mukatibun are assisted in freeing their necks; this is the transmitted interpretation. [...]
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth category of zakat expenditure: 'fi al-riqab' (in the cause of freeing captives). It states the transmitted interpretation is that zakat is given to mukatib (slaves who have a contract of manumission) to help them pay their manumission price. Two possible interpretations are mentioned: (1) purchasing slaves and freeing them, and (2) helping mukatib. The author, following al-Quduri, chooses the second. The reason is that for zakat to be valid, ownership must be transferred to the recipient, and a slave (without a contract) cannot own property. Therefore, giving zakat to buy and free a slave is not valid because the payment is not made to the slave as a owner; rather, it goes to the seller. The correct method is to give directly to the mukatib so he can complete his manumission.

Key Terms
رقاب (riqab): Literally 'necks'; in zakat context, it refers to freeing slaves or assisting mukatib.
مکاتب (mukatib): A slave who has entered a contract (kitabah) with his master to purchase his freedom in installments.
تملیک (tamlik): Granting ownership; a condition for zakat validity that the zakat payment be given as ownership to the recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation in this passage, how should zakat for 'fi al-riqab' be given?
A) By purchasing a slave and freeing him directly.
B) By giving the money to the mukatib to help pay his manumission.
C) By giving it to the master to free the slave.
D) By using it to build a shelter for freed slaves.

Key Takeaway
Zakat for riqab must be given directly to a mukatib to pay his manumission, not used to purchase slaves, because the condition of tamlik requires a capable recipient.

The Zakat Worker's Share: Fixed or by Need?
Dispute on fixed vs need-based Zakat worker's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that the Zakat worker's compensation is by sufficiency (kifaya), explain the Hanafi proof, and distinguish the Hanafi ruling from the Shafi'i fixed-share view.

Core Idea
The Zakat worker's compensation is based on need, not a fixed share, proving it is a fee for work, not Zakat.

The Zakat worker (عامل) is responsible for collecting and distributing Zakat. A key dispute exists between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i: is the worker's compensation a fixed fraction of the Zakat collected, or is it determined by the need arising from his work? This passage presents the Hanafi position and its rational proof, along with an important exception for Hashimi workers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
State the two opposing positions: Shafi'i says fixed one-eighth (or one-seventh), Hanafi says no fixed amount but by sufficiency.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Follow the two arguments: (1) If the owner delivers Zakat directly to the imam, the worker gets nothing -> his entitlement is not from Zakat itself. (2) A wealthy worker can still take his due -> if it were Zakat, he would be ineligible as wealthy recipient.
These point to entitlement by way of work, not by being a Zakat recipient.
3
Analyze the Hashimi exception
Understand why a Hashimi worker cannot take: Zakat funds carry a semblance of charity (shubha), and Hashimis are prohibited from both Zakat and charity. The semblance overrides the work-based entitlement.
The objection: why not also prohibit wealthy non-Hashimi? Answer: honor of Hashimis is higher, so the semblance is considered only for them.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi, the imam can pay the worker more or less than an eighth depending on need. Under Shafi'i, the share is strictly fixed.

کہا ہے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ خداوند قدوس نے زکوۃ کے آٹھ مصارف ذکر فرمائے ہیں تو گویا ہر ایک کا آٹھواں حصہ ہے لہذا عامل کا بھی آٹھواں حصہ متعین ہے یعنی عامل کی کل وصولیابی میں سے آٹھواں حصہ اس کو دیدیا جائے گا اور چونکہ مؤلفۃ القلوب کا حصہ بالا جماع ساقط ہے اس لئے اب سات میں سے ہر ایک کا ساتواں حصہ ہے بہر حال عامل کے لئے ہمارے نزدیک کوئی مقدار متعین نہیں ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک متعین ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عامل کا استحقاق بطریق کفایت ہوتا ہے نہ کہ بطریق زکوۃ چنانچہ صاحب مال نے اگر زکوۃ بذات خود امام کو لا کر دیدی تو عامل قطعاً مستحق نہیں ہوگا اور عامل اگر مالدار ہو اور اس نے کام بھی کیا ہو تو وہ مال زکوۃ میں سے بقدر کفایت اپنا حق لے لے گا اگر عامل کو بطریق زکوۃ دیا جاتا تو مالدار ہونے کی صورت میں وہ مستحق نہ ہوتا پس عامل کا مالدار ہونے کے باوجود لینا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اس کا استحقاق بطریق کفایت ہے نہ کہ بطریق زکوۃ۔
إِلَّا انَّ فِيْه شُهَةَ الصَّدَقَةِ .. الخ سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے اعتراض یہ ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ عامل کا استحقاق بطریق کفایت ہے نہ کہ بطریق زکوۃ تو عامل اگر ہاشمی گھرانے کا ہو تو اس کے لئے بھی بقدر عمل زکوۃ کے مال سے لینا جائز ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ ہاشمی کے لئے بالکل جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ چونکہ زکوۃ ادا کرنے والے کے ذمہ سے زکوۃ ساقط ہوئی ہے اس لئے اس مال میں بھی صدقہ کا شبہ پایا گیا اور جب صدقہ کا شبہ پایا گیا تو خاندان رسالت کو زکوۃ اور صدقہ کے میل و یچیل سے پاک وصاف رکھنے کے لئے ہاشمی عامل کو اس میں سے کچھ نہ دیا جائے گا لیکن اس پر پھر اعتراض ہو گا کہ جس طرح ہاشمی کے لئے زکوۃ کا مال لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے مالدار کے لئے بھی جائز نہیں ہے پس جس طرح ہاشمی عامل نہیں لے گا اسی طرح مالدار عامل کو بھی نہ لینا چاہئے تھا جواب بغیر ہاشمی مالدار مستحق کرامت ہونے میں ہاشمی کے برابر نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے صدقہ کے شبہ کا ہاشمی کے حق میں اعتبار کیا گیا ہے اور غیر ہاشمی مالدار کے حق میں اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔
He said: Imam Shafi'i said that God Almighty mentioned eight recipients of Zakat, so each one's share is an eighth. Therefore, the worker's share is also fixed at an eighth, i.e., from the total collected by the worker, an eighth is given to him. And since the share of those whose hearts are to be reconciled (muallafat al-qulub) is dropped by consensus, now each of the seven gets a seventh. In any case, according to us (Hanafis) there is no fixed amount for the worker, whereas according to Imam Shafi'i it is fixed. Our proof is that the worker's entitlement is by way of sufficiency (kifaya), not by way of Zakat. Thus, if the owner of wealth brings the Zakat to the imam himself, the worker is definitely not entitled. And if the worker is wealthy and has done the work, he will take his right from the Zakat wealth to the extent of sufficiency. If the worker were given by way of Zakat, then in the case of being wealthy he would not be entitled. So the fact that the worker takes despite being wealthy proves that his entitlement is by way of sufficiency, not by way of Zakat. "Except that there is the semblance (shubha) of charity in it..." from this there is an answer to an objection. The objection is: You said that the worker's entitlement is by way of sufficiency, not by way of Zakat. Then if the worker is from the Hashimi family, he should also be allowed to take from Zakat wealth to the extent of his work, whereas it is absolutely not allowed for a Hashimi. The answer: Since the Zakat is dropped from the obligation of the payer, this wealth contains a semblance of charity. When it has a semblance of charity, then to keep the family of the Messenger pure from the mixing and contamination of Zakat and charity, the Hashimi worker will not be given anything from it. But then there is an objection: Just as it is not permissible for a Hashimi to take Zakat wealth, so it should not be permissible for a wealthy person. So just as a Hashimi worker will not take, likewise a wealthy worker should not take. The answer: A non-Hashimi wealthy person cannot be equal to a Hashimi in deserving honor. So the semblance of charity is considered for the Hashimi, but not for the non-Hashimi wealthy person.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding the compensation of the Zakat collector (عامل). Imam Shafi'i holds that the worker's share is a fixed one-eighth of the Zakat proceeds, because Allah enumerated eight categories in Surah al-Tawbah, implying each gets an equal share. The Hanafis argue that the worker's entitlement is not by way of Zakat but by way of sufficiency (kifaya). The proof is that if the owner delivers the Zakat directly to the imam without a worker, the worker gets nothing. Also, a wealthy worker can still take his due, which would not be possible if it were Zakat proper. However, a Hashimi worker cannot take because of the semblance (shubha) of charity in Zakat funds, and Hashimis are prohibited from taking both Zakat and charity. The objection that a wealthy non-Hashimi should also be prohibited is refuted by noting the elevated status of Hashimis.

Key Terms
عامل (aamil): The person appointed to collect Zakat from the wealthy and distribute it.
کفایت (kifāyah): Sufficiency; the amount needed to fulfill the worker's need for his work.
شبهة (shubha): Semblance or doubt; here, the resemblance of Zakat funds to charity due to the discharge of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why can a wealthy Zakat worker still receive compensation?
A) Because he is considered poor relative to the Zakat collected.
B) Because his entitlement is by sufficiency (kifaya), not by way of Zakat.
C) Because he is a descendant of the Prophet.
D) Because the Shafi'i school allows it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Zakat worker's compensation is a fee for work, determined by sufficiency, not a fixed share from the Zakat categories.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

Zakat's 'Fi al-Riqab' – Helping the Mukatib
Clarifies the meaning of 'fi al-riqab' in Zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi interpretation of 'fi al-riqab' in Zakat and explain why purchasing slaves to free does not fulfill the obligation.

Core Idea
Zakat 'fi al-riqab' means assisting the mukatib, not buying slaves – tamlik requires capacity to own.

The fourth category of Zakat expenditure is 'fi al-riqab' (in freeing necks). The Hanafi school, relying on transmitted interpretations from Hasan al-Basri, Imam al-Zuhri, and others, specifies that this refers to helping mukatib slaves pay off their manumission contracts. Understanding this distinction is vital for valid Zakat distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that 'fi al-riqab' is one of the eight categories of Zakat recipients mentioned in Surah al-Tawbah (9:60).
The Arabic phrase 'wa fi al-riqab' literally means 'and in (freeing) necks'.
2
Examine the two interpretations
Note the two forms presented: (1) purchasing a slave and freeing him, (2) helping a mukatib (contracted slave) pay his kitabah.
The author of al-Quduri chose the second form.
3
Apply the transmitted proof
The report from Tabarani quotes Hasan al-Basri, Imam al-Zuhri, and Abdurrahman bin Yazid stating 'fi al-riqab' means the mukatabun.
This is a qawl sahabi with zanni thubut but qati dalala according to the source.
4
Understand the legal condition
Zakat requires tamlik (transfer of ownership) to a recipient who can own. A pure slave cannot own property, so giving Zakat to purchase a slave does not achieve tamlik.
The mukatib, however, has the capacity to own because he is in a contract of manumission.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that 'fi al-riqab' applies exclusively to assisting mukatib slaves; using Zakat to buy and free slaves is invalid.
This is the relied-upon view in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِى الرِّقَابِ أَنْ يُعَانَ الْمُكَاتِبُونَ مِنْهَا فِى فَتِ رِقَابِهِمْ هُوَ الْمَنْقُولُ
ترجمہ اور گردنوں کے چھڑانے میں وہ یہ ہے کہ مکاتبوں کی ان کی گردنوں کے چھڑانے میں اعانت کی جائے یہی تفسیر منقول ہے۔ شریح مصارف زکوۃ کی چوتھی قسم وفی الرقاب ہے اس کی تفسیر میں دو صورتیں بیان کی گئیں میں ایک یہ کہ زکوۃ کے مال سے غلام خرید کر آزاد کیا جائے۔ دوم یہ کہ مکاتب کی بدل کتابت ادا کرنے میں مدد کی جائے۔ صاحب قدوری نے اسی دوسری صورت کو اختیار کیا ہے اور طبرانی میں حسن بصری ، امام زہری اور عبدالرحمن بن یزید بن اسلم سے بھی وفی الرقاب کی یہی تفسیر ہے چنانچہ ان حضرات نے فرمایا ہے وَفِي الرِّقَابِ هُمُ الْمُكَاتُبُونَ يعنى وَفِي الرِّقَابِ سے مراد یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ کی رقم مکاتب کو دیدی جائے تا کہ وہ اپنے مولیٰ کو بدل کتابت ادا کر کے اپنی گردن چھڑا لے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر زکوۃ کی رقم سے غلام خرید کر آزاد کیا جائے تو زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی کیونکہ ادائے زکوۃ کے لئے مالک کر دینا شرط ہے اور اس صورت میں مالک کو دینے کے معنی نہیں پائے گئے کیونکہ خالص غلام کے اندر مالک بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔
And regarding necks (al-riqab): that the mukatibun are helped from it in the [؟] of their necks – this is the transmitted interpretation. Translation: In freeing necks, it is that the mukatibs are assisted in freeing their necks – this is the transmitted interpretation. Sharh[؟]: The fourth category of Zakat expenditures is 'fi al-riqab'. In its interpretation, two forms are mentioned: one is that a slave is purchased and freed from Zakat wealth; the second is that a mukatib is helped in paying his kitaba. The author of al-Quduri adopted the second form. And in al-Tabrani, from Hasan al-Basri, Imam al-Zuhri, and Abdurrahman bin Yazid bin Aslam, this same interpretation of 'fi al-riqab' is narrated. Thus, those scholars said: 'Fi al-riqab' means the mukatibun. That is, the intended meaning of 'fi al-riqab' is that Zakat money is given to the mukatib so that he can pay his master the kitaba and free his neck. From this it is known that if a slave is purchased and freed from Zakat money, the Zakat is not fulfilled, because for the performance of Zakat, transferring ownership (tamlik) is a condition, and in this case the meaning of giving to an owner is not found, because a pure slave does not have the capacity to be an owner.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi interpretation of the fourth category of Zakat recipients: 'fi al-riqab' (in freeing necks). The preferred view, based on the narration of Hasan al-Basri, Imam Zuhri, and Abdurrahman bin Yazid, is that it refers to helping mukatib slaves (those who have a contract of manumission with their masters) by giving them Zakat funds to pay off their contracts. The alternative view of buying slaves to free them is rejected because Zakat requires tamlik (transfer of ownership), and a slave cannot be made owner of the Zakat since he himself is owned. Therefore, giving Zakat to the mukatib is valid because the mukatib is a recipient who can own the money and then use it to pay his master.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered a contract with his master to pay a certain amount in exchange for manumission.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitābah): The agreed-upon payment in the manumission contract that the mukatib must pay to his master.
رقاب (riqāb): Literally 'necks', used metaphorically for slaves; in Zakat context, specifically mukatibun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the Hanafi interpretation, to whom should Zakat money be given under the category 'fi al-riqab'?
A) To a slave owner to free his slave.
B) To a mukatib slave to pay his manumission contract.
C) To a poor person.
D) To a traveler.

Key Takeaway
Zakat's 'fi al-riqab' category is specifically for helping mukatib slaves, not for purchasing slaves, due to the condition of tamlik.

Definition of Gharim (Debtor) – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Defines gharim as a debtor with no surplus Nisab; contrasts Shafi'i view on reconciling parties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of gharim for Zakat eligibility and explain the key difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
A debtor qualifies for Zakat only if his net wealth after debt is below Nisab.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of gharim (debtor) as a category of Zakat recipients. The passage from al-Quduri, as explained in al-Hidayah, distinguishes the Hanafi view from that of Imam al-Shafi'i. You will learn the precise condition under which a debtor is eligible and understand the practical consequence of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi definition of gharim: a person liable for a debt and who does not own a surplus Nisab over that debt.
The example given: 1000 dirhams cash, 900 dirhams debt leaves 100 dirhams (< Nisab).
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i includes those who incur financial liability for reconciliation between people, even if they remain wealthy.
This is an expansion of the category beyond simple poverty.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: such a person is not eligible unless he becomes poor after spending; then he is faqir, not gharim.
The distinction: gharim requires net wealth below Nisab; reconciliation alone does not create eligibility.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a wealthy reconciliation spender can take Zakat according to Shafi'i, but not according to Hanafi.
In the Hanafi school, Zakat is strictly for the needy, not for rewarding good deeds.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.
This is based on the reasoning that debt reduces effective ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعَارِمُ مَنْ لَزِمَهُ دَينُ وَلَا يَمْلِكُ نِصَابًا فَاضِلَّا عَنْ دَيْبِهِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ مَنْ تَحَمَّلَ غَرَامَةً فِي إِصْلَاحِ ذَاتِ الْبَيْنِ وإطفاء النَّائِرَة بَيْنَ الْقَبْيلَتَين
ترجمہ اور غارم وہ شخص ہے جس پر قرضہ لازم ہو اور اپنے قرضہ سے فاضل کسی نصاب کا مالک نہ ہو اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ غارم وہ ہے جس نے مسلمانوں کے درمیان باہمی پھوٹ کی اصلاح کی خاطر اور دو قبیلوں کے درمیان عداوت کی آگ کو بجھانے کے لئے مالی خسارہ برداشت کیا ہو۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری کے بیان کے مطابق مصارف زکوۃ کی پانچویں قسم غارم ہے غارم وہ شخص ہے جس کے ذمہ لوگوں کا قرضہ ہو ۔ اور قرضہ سے فاضل مقدار نصاب کا مالک نہ ہو ۔ مثلا ایک آدمی سپاس ایک ہزار درہم ہوں اور وہ نوسو درہم کا مقروض ہو تو اس کو زکوۃ دینا جائز ہے کیونکہ نوسو درہم کے ساتھ قرض خواہوں کا حق متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ تو معدوم ہو گئے یعنی یہ نو سودرہم گویا اس کی ملک نہ رہے اور رہے ہو در همر تو وہ بقدر نصاب نہیں ہیں۔ اس لئے اس کے واسطے زکوۃ کا مال لینا جائز ہوگا ۔ امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ غارم وہ شخص ہے جس نے دو متحارب مسلم گروہوں کے درمیان صلح کرانے اور دشمنی کی آگ بجھانے کی خاطر کچھ مالی خسارہ برداشت کیا تو شخص اگر چہ مالدار ہو لیکن اس مقصد کے لئے زکوۃ لے سکتا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک یہ شخص زکوۃ نہیں لے سکتا ۔ ہاں اگر اصلاح بین الناس پر خرچ کرنے کے بعد مقدار نصاب کا مالک نہ رہا ہو تو لے سکتا ہے مگر یہ لینا غارم کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ فقیر یعنی مقدار نصاب کا مالک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے۔
And al-gharim is the one whom a debt has become incumbent, and he does not own a surplus Nisab over his debt. And al-Shafi'i said: the one who incurred a financial liability for the reform of relations among people and extinguishing the fire [of discord] between two tribes. Translation: And gharim is the person who is liable for a debt and does not own a Nisab surplus over his debt. And Imam Shafi'i said: gharim is the one who incurred a financial loss for the reform of relations among people and extinguishing the fire of enmity between two tribes. Explanation: According to the statement of Sahib al-Quduri, the fifth category of Zakat expenditures is gharim. Gharim is the person who owes a debt to people and does not own a Nisab surplus over his debt. For example, a person has one thousand dirhams and he owes nine hundred dirhams: giving him Zakat is permissible, because due to the right of the creditors being attached to the nine hundred dirhams, they are nonexistent, i.e., these nine hundred dirhams are as if no longer his property, and the remaining one hundred dirhams are not equal to Nisab. Therefore, taking Zakat wealth for him is permissible. Imam Shafi'i says: gharim is the person who incurred some financial loss for the sake of making peace between two warring Muslim groups and extinguishing the fire of enmity. So even if the person is wealthy, he can take Zakat for this purpose. And according to us, this person cannot take Zakat. Yes, if after spending on reform between people he does not own a Nisab, then he can take, but this taking is not due to being gharim, but due to being faqir, i.e., not owning Nisab.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi definition of gharim (debtor) as a recipient of Zakat. According to the Hanafi school, a gharim is a person who is in debt and after paying the debt does not have enough wealth to reach the Nisab. For example, if someone has 1000 dirhams but owes 900, he is eligible because 900 are effectively not his property (due to creditors' rights), and the remaining 100 is below Nisab. Imam Shafi'i expands the definition to include those who take on financial liability for reconciliation between Muslims, even if they are wealthy. The Hanafis disagree; such a person is only eligible if he becomes poor after spending, but then he qualifies as faqir, not gharim. This reflects the Hanafi principle that Zakat is for the needy, not for rewarding good deeds.

Key Terms
غارم (ghārim): A person who is indebted and whose net wealth after deducting debt is less than Nisab.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth that makes Zakat obligatory on the owner; also the threshold for being considered rich.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following qualifies as gharim for receiving Zakat?
A) A wealthy person who incurred debt to reconcile two tribes.
B) A person with 1000 dirhams owing 900 dirhams.
C) A person with 200 dirhams and no debt.
D) A person with 1000 dirhams owing 100 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of gharim requires that the debtor's net wealth after debt is less than Nisab; the Shafi'i inclusion of reconciliation debt is not accepted.
